      <p><b>Algeria</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/dʒ/: 'j' in 'jam'">dʒ</span><span title="/ɪər/: 'ear' in 'near'">ɪər</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Algeria-pronunciation.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/16/En-Algeria-pronunciation.ogg" class="internal" title="En-Algeria-pronunciation.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling">al-<span style="font-size:90%">JEER</span>-ee-ə</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a>: Lezzayer <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الجزائر</span>‎ <i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization"><i>al-Jazā'ir</i></i>), officially the <b>People's Democratic Republic of Algeria</b>, is a country in the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> region of <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>. The capital and most populous city is <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, located in the far north of the country on the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> coast. With an area of 2,381,741 square kilometres (919,595&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), Algeria is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">tenth-largest country in the world</a>, and the largest by area in the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> With an estimated population of over 44 million, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_countries_by_population" title="List of African countries by population">ninth-most populous country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. </p>
      <p>Algeria is bordered to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Tunisia_border" title="Algeria–Tunisia border">the northeast</a> by <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Libya_border" title="Algeria–Libya border">the east</a> by <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Niger_border" title="Algeria–Niger border">the southeast</a> by <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Western_Sahara_border" title="Algeria–Western Sahara border">the southwest</a> by <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Saharan</a> territory, to <a href="/wiki/Algeria%E2%80%93Morocco_border" title="Algeria–Morocco border">the west</a> by <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>, and to the north by the Mediterranean Sea. The country has a semi-arid geography, with most of the population living in the fertile north and the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a> dominating the geography of the south. This arid geography makes the country <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Algeria" title="Climate change in Algeria">very vulnerable to climate change.</a><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Pre-1962 Algeria has known many empires and dynasties, including ancient <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punics" title="Punics">Carthaginians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vandal_Kingdom" title="Vandal Kingdom">Vandals</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate" title="Abbasid Caliphate">Abbasids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rustamid_dynasty" title="Rustamid dynasty">Rustamid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idrisid_dynasty" title="Idrisid dynasty">Idrisid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aghlabids" title="Aghlabids">Aghlabids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zirid_dynasty" title="Zirid dynasty">Zirid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hammadid_dynasty" title="Hammadid dynasty">Hammadids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohads</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">Zayyanids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spaniards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottomans</a> and finally, the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a>. Most of the population is <a href="/wiki/Arab-Berber" title="Arab-Berber">Arab-Berber</a>, practicing <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Algeria" title="Islam in Algeria">Islam</a> and using the official languages of <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a>. However, <a href="/wiki/French_language_in_Algeria" title="French language in Algeria">French</a> serves as an administrative and education language in some contexts, and <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a> is the main spoken language. </p>
      <p>Algeria has a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential republic</a>, with local constituencies consisting of 58 provinces and 1,541 communes. Algeria is a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middle_power" title="Middle power">middle power</a>. It has the highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> of all non-island African countries and one of the largest economies on the continent, based largely on energy exports. Algeria has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">16th largest</a> oil reserves in the world and the second largest in Africa, while it has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">ninth largest reserves</a> of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, the national oil company, is the largest company in Africa, supplying large amounts of <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a> to Europe. Algeria has one of the largest militaries in Africa and the largest defence budget. It is a member of the African Union, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union" title="Arab Maghreb Union">Arab Maghreb Union</a>, of which it is a founding member. </p>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-27"><a href="#Health"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Health</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">7.5</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Cities"><span class="tocnumber">7.6</span> <span class="toctext">Cities</span></a></li> 
         </ul> </li> 
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a> 
         <ul> 
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Media"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Media</span></a></li>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Music"><span class="tocnumber">8.4</span> <span class="toctext">Music</span></a></li>

       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Other forms of the name are: <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الجزائر</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Jazāʾir</i>, <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian Arabic language">Algerian Arabic</a>: <span lang="arq" dir="rtl">الدزاير</span>‎, <small>romanized:&nbsp;</small><i lang="arq-Latn" title="Algerian Arabic-language romanization">al-dzāyīr</i>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Algérie</i>. It is officially the <b>People's Democratic Republic of Algeria</b> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الجمهورية الجزائرية الديمقراطية الشعبية</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-Jumhūriyya al-Jazāʾiriyya ad-Dīmuqrāṭiyya aš-Šaʿbiyya</i>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">République algérienne démocratique et populaire</i>, abbreviated as RADP). </p>
      <p>The country's name derives from the city of <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> which in turn derives from the Arabic <i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language text">al-Jazāʾir</i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic-language text">الجزائر</span>, "The Islands"),<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> a truncated form of the older <i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language text">Jazāʾir Banī Mazghanna</i> (<span lang="ar" dir="rtl" title="Arabic-language text">جزائر بني مزغنة</span>, "Islands of the Mazghanna Tribe"),<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-idrisi_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-idrisi-14">[13]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-khaldun_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-khaldun-15">[14]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> employed by medieval geographers such as <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_al-Idrisi" title="Muhammad al-Idrisi">al-Idrisi</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Algeria" title="History of Algeria">History of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory_and_ancient_history">Prehistory and ancient history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory and ancient history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prehistoric_North_Africa" title="Prehistoric North Africa">Prehistoric North Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Africa_during_Antiquity" title="North Africa during Antiquity">North Africa during Antiquity</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg/220px-Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg/330px-Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg/440px-Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="501"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dj%C3%A9mila-109038.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roman ruins at <a href="/wiki/Dj%C3%A9mila" title="Djémila">Djémila</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the region of Ain Hanech (<a href="/wiki/Sa%C3%AFda_Province" title="Saïda Province">Saïda Province</a>), early remnants (200,000 BC) of hominid occupation in <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a> were found. Neanderthal tool makers produced hand axes in the <a href="/wiki/Levallois_technique" title="Levallois technique">Levalloisian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mousterian" title="Mousterian">Mousterian</a> styles (43,000 BC) similar to those in the <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup> Algeria was the site of the highest state of development of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">Middle Paleolithic</a> <a href="/wiki/Flake_tool" title="Flake tool">Flake tool</a> techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-DelsonTattersall2004_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DelsonTattersall2004-18">[17]</a></sup> Tools of this era, starting about 30,000 BC, are called <a href="/wiki/Aterian" title="Aterian">Aterian</a> (after the archaeological site of <a href="/wiki/Bir_el_Ater" title="Bir el Ater">Bir el Ater</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9bessa" title="Tébessa">Tebessa</a>). </p>
      <p>The earliest blade industries in North Africa are called <a href="/wiki/Iberomaurusian" title="Iberomaurusian">Iberomaurusian</a> (located mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> region). This industry appears to have spread throughout the coastal regions of the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> between 15,000 and 10,000 BC. Neolithic civilization (animal domestication and agriculture) developed in the Saharan and Mediterranean Maghreb perhaps as early as 11,000 BC<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> or as late as between 6000 and 2000 BC. This life, richly depicted in the <a href="/wiki/Tassili_n%27Ajjer" title="Tassili n'Ajjer">Tassili n'Ajjer</a> paintings, predominated in Algeria until the classical period. The mixture of peoples of North Africa coalesced eventually into a distinct native population that came to be called <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Berbers</a>, who are the indigenous peoples of northern Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Timgad_rue.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Timgad_rue.jpg/220px-Timgad_rue.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Timgad_rue.jpg/330px-Timgad_rue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Timgad_rue.jpg/440px-Timgad_rue.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Timgad_rue.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ancient <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> ruins of <a href="/wiki/Timgad" title="Timgad">Timgadon</a> the street leading to the local <a href="/wiki/Arch_of_Trajan_(Timgad)" title="Arch of Trajan (Timgad)">Arch of Trajan</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From their principal center of power at <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Carthaginians" class="mw-redirect" title="Carthaginians">Carthaginians</a> expanded and established small settlements along the North African coast; by 600 BC, a <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> presence existed at <a href="/wiki/Tipasa" title="Tipasa">Tipasa</a>, east of <a href="/wiki/Cherchell" title="Cherchell">Cherchell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hippo_Regius" title="Hippo Regius">Hippo Regius</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Rusicade" class="mw-redirect" title="Rusicade">Rusicade</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Skikda" title="Skikda">Skikda</a>). These settlements served as market towns as well as anchorages. </p>
      <p>As Carthaginian power grew, its impact on the indigenous population increased dramatically. Berber civilisation was already at a stage in which agriculture, manufacturing, trade, and political organisation supported several states. Trade links between Carthage and the Berbers in the interior grew, but territorial expansion also resulted in the enslavement or military recruitment of some Berbers and in the extraction of tribute from others. </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:408px;max-width:408px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:GM_Massinissa.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/GM_Massinissa.png/200px-GM_Massinissa.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/GM_Massinissa.png/300px-GM_Massinissa.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/GM_Massinissa.png/400px-GM_Massinissa.png 2x" data-file-width="865" data-file-height="862"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Masinissa" title="Masinissa">Masinissa</a> (c.&nbsp;238–148&nbsp;BC), first king of Numidia
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Jugurtha.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/72/Jugurtha.JPG" decoding="async" width="200" height="200" data-file-width="184" data-file-height="184"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Jugurtha" title="Jugurtha">Jugurtha</a> (c.&nbsp;160–104&nbsp;BC), king of Numidia
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>By the early 4th century BC, Berbers formed the single largest element of the Carthaginian army. In the <a href="/wiki/Mercenary_War" title="Mercenary War">Revolt of the Mercenaries</a>, Berber soldiers rebelled from 241 to 238 BC after being unpaid following the defeat of Carthage in the <a href="/wiki/First_Punic_War" title="First Punic War">First Punic War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Fischer-Bovet2014_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fischer-Bovet2014-21">[20]</a></sup> They succeeded in obtaining control of much of Carthage's North African territory, and they minted coins bearing the name Libyan, used in Greek to describe natives of North Africa. The Carthaginian state declined because of successive defeats by the Romans in the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Spielvogel2014_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spielvogel2014-22">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 146 BC the city of <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a> was destroyed. As Carthaginian power waned, the influence of Berber leaders in the hinterland grew. By the 2nd century BC, several large but loosely administered Berber kingdoms had emerged. Two of them were established in <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidia</a>, behind the coastal areas controlled by Carthage. West of Numidia lay <a href="/wiki/Mauretania" title="Mauretania">Mauretania</a>, which extended across the <a href="/wiki/Moulouya_River" title="Moulouya River">Moulouya River</a> in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> to the Atlantic Ocean. The high point of Berber civilization, unequaled until the coming of the <a href="/wiki/Almohads" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a> more than a millennium later, was reached during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Masinissa" title="Masinissa">Masinissa</a> in the 2nd century BC. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Egypt,_Rome,_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Egypt%2C_Rome%2C_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg/220px-Egypt%2C_Rome%2C_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Egypt%2C_Rome%2C_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg/330px-Egypt%2C_Rome%2C_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Egypt%2C_Rome%2C_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg/440px-Egypt%2C_Rome%2C_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2360" data-file-height="1924"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Egypt,_Rome,_Carthage_and_Numidia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidia</a> along with <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom" title="Ptolemaic Kingdom">Egypt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Rome</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthage</a> 200 BC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After Masinissa's death in 148 BC, the Berber kingdoms were divided and reunited several times. Masinissa's line survived until 24 AD, when the remaining Berber territory was annexed to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. </p>
      <p>For several centuries Algeria was ruled by the Romans, who founded many colonies in the region. Like the rest of North Africa, Algeria was one of the breadbaskets of the empire, exporting cereals and other agricultural products. <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Saint Augustine</a> was the bishop of <a href="/wiki/Hippo_Regius" title="Hippo Regius">Hippo Regius</a> (modern-day Annaba, Algeria), located in the Roman province of <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">Africa</a>. The Germanic <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> of <a href="/wiki/Geiseric" class="mw-redirect" title="Geiseric">Geiseric</a> moved into North Africa in 429, and by 435 controlled coastal Numidia.<sup id="cite_ref-vandaf_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vandaf-23">[22]</a></sup> They did not make any significant settlement on the land, as they were harassed by local tribes. In fact, by the time the Byzantines arrived <a href="/wiki/Leptis_Magna" title="Leptis Magna">Leptis Magna</a> was abandoned and the Msellata region was occupied by the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Amazigh" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazigh">Laguatan</a> who had been busy facilitating an <a href="/wiki/Amazigh" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazigh">Amazigh</a> political, military and cultural revival.<sup id="cite_ref-vandaf_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vandaf-23">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Medieval_Muslim_Algeria" title="Medieval Muslim Algeria">Medieval Muslim Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Mansourah-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mansourah-1.jpg/220px-Mansourah-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mansourah-1.jpg/330px-Mansourah-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Mansourah-1.jpg/440px-Mansourah-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Mansourah-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mansourah mosque, Tlemcen
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> After negligible resistance from the locals, <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslim</a> <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a> conquered Algeria in the early 8th century. </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_(Algeria).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg/200px-Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="364" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg/300px-Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg/400px-Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_%28Algeria%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="738" data-file-height="1344"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Dyhia_in_Khenchela_(Algeria).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Dihya" title="Dihya">Dihya</a> memorial in <a href="/wiki/Khenchela" title="Khenchela">Khenchela</a>, Algeria
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p> Large numbers of the indigenous Berber people converted to Islam. Christians, Berber and Latin speakers remained in the great majority in Tunisia until the end of the 9th century and Muslims only became a vast majority some time in the 10th.<sup id="cite_ref-jonathan_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jonathan-25">[24]</a></sup> After the fall of the Umayyad Caliphate, numerous local dynasties emerged, including the <a href="/wiki/Rustamids" class="mw-redirect" title="Rustamids">Rustamids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aghlabids" title="Aghlabids">Aghlabids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fatimids" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zirids" class="mw-redirect" title="Zirids">Zirids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hammadids" class="mw-redirect" title="Hammadids">Hammadids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almohads" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Abdalwadid" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdalwadid">Abdalwadid</a>. The Christians left in three waves: after the initial conquest, in the 10th century and the 11th. The last were evacuated to Sicily by the Normans and the few remaining died out in the 14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-jonathan_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jonathan-25">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, North Africa was home to many great scholars, saints and sovereigns including <a href="/wiki/Judah_ibn_Kuraish" title="Judah ibn Kuraish">Judah Ibn Quraysh</a>, the first grammarian to mention Semitic and Berber languages, the great Sufi masters <a href="/wiki/Abu_Madyan" title="Abu Madyan">Sidi Boumediene (Abu Madyan)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sidi_El_Houari" title="Sidi El Houari">Sidi El Houari</a>, and the Emirs <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu'min">Abd Al Mu'min</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yaghmurasen_Ibn_Zyan" title="Yaghmurasen Ibn Zyan">Yāghmūrasen</a>. It was during this time that the <a href="/wiki/Fatimids" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimids">Fatimids</a> or children of Fatima, daughter of Muhammad, came to the Maghreb. These "Fatimids" went on to found a long lasting dynasty stretching across the Maghreb, Hejaz and the Levant, boasting a secular inner government, as well as a powerful army and navy, made up primarily of <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levantines</a> extending from Algeria to their capital state of <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_caliphate" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimid caliphate">Fatimid caliphate</a> began to collapse when its governors the <a href="/wiki/Zirids" class="mw-redirect" title="Zirids">Zirids</a> seceded. In order to punish them the Fatimids sent the Arab <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banu_Sulaym" title="Banu Sulaym">Banu Sulaym</a> against them. The resultant war is recounted in the epic <a href="/wiki/Taghribat_Bani_Hilal" title="Taghribat Bani Hilal">Tāghribāt</a>. In Al-Tāghrībāt the Amazigh Zirid Hero <a href="/wiki/Khalifa_al-Zanati" title="Khalifa al-Zanati">Khālīfā Al-Zānatī</a> asks daily, for duels, to defeat the Hilalan hero <a href="/wiki/Abu_Zayd_al-Hilali" title="Abu Zayd al-Hilali">Ābu Zayd al-Hilalī</a> and many other Arab knights in a string of victories. The <a href="/wiki/Zirid" class="mw-redirect" title="Zirid">Zirids</a>, however, were ultimately defeated ushering in an adoption of Arab customs and culture. The indigenous <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Amazigh</a> tribes, however, remained largely independent, and depending on tribe, location and time controlled varying parts of the Maghreb, at times unifying it (as under the Fatimids). The Fatimid Islamic state, also known as <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid Caliphate</a> made an Islamic empire that included North Africa, Sicily, <a href="/wiki/Palestine_(region)" title="Palestine (region)">Palestine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> coast of Africa, Tihamah, <a href="/wiki/Hejaz" title="Hejaz">Hejaz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> Caliphates from Northern Africa traded with the other empires of their time, as well as forming part of a confederated support and trade network with other Islamic states during the Islamic Era. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Fatimid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fatimid.jpg/220px-Fatimid.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="123" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fatimid.jpg/330px-Fatimid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Fatimid.jpg/440px-Fatimid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3466" data-file-height="1931"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Fatimid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Fatimid Caliphate, a <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> <a href="/wiki/Isma%27ilism" title="Isma'ilism">Ismaili</a> dynasty that ruled much of North Africa, c. 960–1100
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Amazighs</a> historically consisted of several tribes. The two main branches were the Botr and Barnès tribes, who were divided into tribes, and again into sub-tribes. Each region of the Maghreb contained several tribes (for example, <a href="/wiki/Sanhadja" class="mw-redirect" title="Sanhadja">Sanhadja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Houara" class="mw-redirect" title="Houara">Houara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zenata" title="Zenata">Zenata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Masmuda" title="Masmuda">Masmouda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kutama" title="Kutama">Kutama</a>, Awarba, and <a href="/wiki/Berghwata" class="mw-redirect" title="Berghwata">Berghwata</a>). All these tribes made independent territorial decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several <a href="/wiki/Berber_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber people">Amazigh</a> dynasties emerged during the Middle Ages in the Maghreb and other nearby lands. <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a> provides a table summarising the Amazigh dynasties of the Maghreb region, the <a href="/wiki/Zirid_dynasty" title="Zirid dynasty">Zirid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banu_Ifran" title="Banu Ifran">Banu Ifran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maghrawa" title="Maghrawa">Maghrawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almoravid" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravid">Almoravid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hammadid" class="mw-redirect" title="Hammadid">Hammadid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almohad" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohad">Almohad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Merinid" class="mw-redirect" title="Merinid">Merinid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zayyanid_dynasty" title="Zayyanid dynasty">Abdalwadid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wattasid" class="mw-redirect" title="Wattasid">Wattasid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meknassa" class="mw-redirect" title="Meknassa">Meknassa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hafsid" class="mw-redirect" title="Hafsid">Hafsid</a> dynasties.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Empire_almohade.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_almohade.PNG/220px-Empire_almohade.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_almohade.PNG/330px-Empire_almohade.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_almohade.PNG/440px-Empire_almohade.PNG 2x" data-file-width="882" data-file-height="648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Empire_almohade.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The Berber <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohad Caliphate</a> at its greatest extent, c.&nbsp;1212
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There reigned in <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">Ifriqiya</a>, current Tunisia, a <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berber</a> family, <a href="/wiki/Zirid_dynasty" title="Zirid dynasty">Zirid</a>, somehow recognising the suzerainty of the <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid</a> caliph of <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>. Probably in 1048, the Zirid ruler or viceroy, el-Mu'izz, decided to end this suzerainty. The <a href="/wiki/Fatimid" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimid">Fatimid</a> state was too weak to attempt a punitive expedition; The Viceroy, el-Mu'izz, also found another means of revenge. </p>
      <p>Between the <a href="/wiki/Nile" title="Nile">Nile</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Sea" title="Red Sea">Red Sea</a> were living <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> tribes expelled from <a href="/wiki/Arabia" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabia">Arabia</a> for their disruption and turbulent influence, both <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banu_Sulaym" title="Banu Sulaym">Banu Sulaym</a> among others, whose presence disrupted farmers in the <a href="/wiki/Nile_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="Nile Valley">Nile Valley</a> since the nomads would often loot. The then <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">Fatimid</a> vizier devised to relinquish control of the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> and obtained the agreement of his sovereign. This not only prompted the Bedouins to leave, but the <a href="/wiki/Fatimid" class="mw-redirect" title="Fatimid">Fatimid</a> treasury even gave them a light expatriation cash allowance. </p>
      <p>Whole tribes set off with women, children, ancestors, animals and camping equipment. Some stopped on the way, especially in <a href="/wiki/Cyrenaica" title="Cyrenaica">Cyrenaica</a>, where they are still one of the essential elements of the settlement but most arrived in <a href="/wiki/Ifriqiya" title="Ifriqiya">Ifriqiya</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Gab%C3%A8s_Governorate" title="Gabès Governorate">Gabes</a> region. The <a href="/wiki/Zirid" class="mw-redirect" title="Zirid">Zirid</a> ruler tried to stop this rising tide, but with each encounter, the last under the walls of <a href="/wiki/Kairouan" title="Kairouan">Kairouan</a>, his troops were defeated and the Arabs remained masters of the field. </p>
      <p>The flood was still rising, and in 1057, the Arabs spread on the high plains of <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Algeria" title="Constantine, Algeria">Constantine</a> where they gradually choked <a href="/wiki/Beni_Hammad_Fort" title="Beni Hammad Fort">Qalaa of Banu Hammad</a>, as they had done in Kairouan a few decades ago. From there they gradually gained the upper <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> plains. Some were forcibly taken by the <a href="/wiki/Almohads" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohads">Almohads</a> in the second half of the 12th century. We can say that in the 13th century the Arabs were in all of <a href="/wiki/North_Africa" title="North Africa">North Africa</a>, with the exception of the main mountain ranges and certain coastal regions which remained entirely Berber.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Verification needed for 13th century comment that">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The influx of <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> tribes was a major factor in the linguistic, cultural <a href="/wiki/Arabization" title="Arabization">Arabization</a> of the Maghreb and in the spread of <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadism</a> in areas where <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> had previously been dominant.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a> noted that the lands ravaged by <a href="/wiki/Banu_Hilal" title="Banu Hilal">Banu Hilal</a> tribes had become completely arid desert.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> constructed fortified outposts (<a href="/wiki/Presidio" title="Presidio">presidios</a>) on or near the Algerian coast. <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> took control of few coastal towns like <a href="/wiki/Mers_el_Kebir" class="mw-redirect" title="Mers el Kebir">Mers el Kebir</a> in 1505; <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> in 1509; and <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mostaganem" title="Mostaganem">Mostaganem</a> and <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9n%C3%A8s" title="Ténès">Ténès</a> in 1510. In the same year, a few merchants of Algiers ceded one of the rocky islets in their harbour to Spain, which built a fort on it. The presidios in North Africa turned out to be a costly and largely ineffective military endeavour that did not guarantee access for Spain's merchant fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ottoman_era">Ottoman era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ottoman era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Algeria" title="Ottoman Algeria">Ottoman Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maghreb_15th_Century.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Maghreb_15th_Century.svg/220px-Maghreb_15th_Century.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="83" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Maghreb_15th_Century.svg/330px-Maghreb_15th_Century.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Maghreb_15th_Century.svg/440px-Maghreb_15th_Century.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3127" data-file-height="1185"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maghreb_15th_Century.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tlemcen" title="Kingdom of Tlemcen">Zayyanid kingdom</a> of Tlemcen in the fifteenth century and its neighbors
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The region of Algeria was partially ruled by <a href="/wiki/Ottomans" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottomans">Ottomans</a> for three centuries from 1516 to 1830. In 1516 the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turkish</a> privateer brothers <a href="/wiki/Aruj" class="mw-redirect" title="Aruj">Aruj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin Barbarossa</a>, who operated successfully under the <a href="/wiki/Hafsids" class="mw-redirect" title="Hafsids">Hafsids</a>, moved their base of operations to Algiers. They succeeded in conquering Jijel and Algiers from the <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spaniards</a> but eventually assumed control over the city and the surrounding region, forcing the previous ruler, Abu Hamo Musa III of the <i>Bani Ziyad</i> dynasty, to flee. When Aruj was killed in 1518 during his invasion of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tlemcen" title="Kingdom of Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a>, Hayreddin succeeded him as military commander of Algiers. The <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> sultan gave him the title of <a href="/wiki/Beylerbey" title="Beylerbey">beylerbey</a> and a contingent of some 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Janissaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Janissaries">janissaries</a>. With the aid of this force, <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin</a> conquered the whole area between Constantine and Oran (although the city of Oran remained in Spanish hands until 1792).<sup id="cite_ref-csa16_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-34">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mikaberidze_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mikaberidze-35">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg/220px-Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg/330px-Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg/440px-Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg 2x" data-file-width="572" data-file-height="787"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Barbarossa_Hayreddin_Pasha.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin Barbarossa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The next beylerbey was Hayreddin's son <a href="/wiki/Hasan_Pasha_(son_of_Barbarossa)" title="Hasan Pasha (son of Barbarossa)">Hasan</a>, who assumed the position in 1544. Until 1587 the area was governed by officers who served terms with no fixed limits. Subsequently, with the institution of a regular Ottoman administration, governors with the title of pasha ruled for three-year terms. The pasha was assisted by janissaries, known in Algeria as the ojaq and led by an <a href="/wiki/Agha_(Ottoman_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Agha (Ottoman Empire)">agha</a>. Discontent among the ojaq rose in the mid-1600s because they were not paid regularly, and they repeatedly revolted against the pasha. As a result, the agha charged the pasha with corruption and incompetence and seized power in 1659.<sup id="cite_ref-csa16_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-34">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Plague_(disease)" title="Plague (disease)">Plague</a> had repeatedly struck the cities of North Africa. Algiers lost from 30,000 to 50,000 inhabitants to the plague in 1620–21, and suffered high fatalities in 1654–57, 1665, 1691 and 1740–42.<sup id="cite_ref-Davis_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-36">[35]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1671, the <a href="/wiki/Taifa" title="Taifa">taifa</a> rebelled, killed the agha, and placed one of its own in power. The new leader received the title of <a href="/wiki/Dey" title="Dey">Dey</a>. After 1689, the right to select the dey passed to the <a href="/wiki/Divan" title="Divan">divan</a>, a council of some sixty nobles. It was at first dominated by the <i><a href="/wiki/Ojaq" title="Ojaq">ojaq</a></i>; but by the 18th century, it had become the dey's instrument. In 1710, the dey persuaded the sultan to recognise him and his successors as regent, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Pasha" title="Pasha">pasha</a> in that role, although Algiers remained a part of the Ottoman Empire.<sup id="cite_ref-csa16_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-34">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The dey was in effect a constitutional autocrat. The dey was elected for a life term, but in the 159 years (1671–1830) that the system survived, fourteen of the twenty-nine deys were assassinated. Despite usurpation, military coups and occasional mob rule, the day-to-day operation of Ottoman government was remarkably orderly. Although the regency patronised the tribal chieftains, it never had the unanimous allegiance of the countryside, where heavy taxation frequently provoked unrest. Autonomous tribal states were tolerated, and the regency's authority was seldom applied in the <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-csa16_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csa16-34">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG/220px-Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG/330px-Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG/440px-Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1121" data-file-height="839"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Debarquement_et_maltraitement_de_prisonniers_a_alger.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Slavery in the Ottoman Empire">Christian slaves</a> in Algiers, 1706
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirates" title="Barbary pirates">Barbary pirates</a> preyed on Christian and other non-Islamic shipping in the western Mediterranean Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-Davis_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davis-36">[35]</a></sup> The pirates often took the passengers and crew on the ships and sold them or used them as <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">slaves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hannay_1911_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hannay_1911-37">[36]</a></sup> They also did a brisk business in ransoming some of the captives. According to Robert Davis, from the 16th to 19th century, pirates captured 1 million to 1.25 million Europeans as slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-barbary_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-barbary-38">[37]</a></sup> They often made raids, called <a href="/wiki/Ghazi_(warrior)" title="Ghazi (warrior)">Razzias</a>, on European coastal towns to capture Christian slaves to sell at <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Slavery in the Ottoman Empire">slave markets</a> in North Africa and other parts of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> In 1544, for example, <a href="/wiki/Hayreddin_Barbarossa" title="Hayreddin Barbarossa">Hayreddin Barbarossa</a> captured the island of <a href="/wiki/Ischia" title="Ischia">Ischia</a>, taking 4,000 prisoners, and enslaved some 9,000 inhabitants of <a href="/wiki/Lipari" title="Lipari">Lipari</a>, almost the entire population.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> In 1551, the Ottoman governor of Algiers, <a href="/wiki/Turgut_Reis" class="mw-redirect" title="Turgut Reis">Turgut Reis</a>, enslaved the entire population of the <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Maltese</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Gozo" title="Gozo">Gozo</a>. Barbary pirates often attacked the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>. The threat was so severe that residents abandoned the island of <a href="/wiki/Formentera" title="Formentera">Formentera</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> The introduction of broad-sail ships from the beginning of the 17th century allowed them to branch out into the Atlantic.<sup id="cite_ref-Auchterlonie2012_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Auchterlonie2012-43">[42]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/220px-thumbnail.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/330px-thumbnail.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven%2C_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg/440px-thumbnail.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2940" data-file-height="2061"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:De_Engels-Nederlandse_vloot_in_de_Baai_van_Algiers_ter_ondersteuning_van_het_ultimatum_tot_vrijlating_van_blanke_slaven,_26_augustus_1816._Rijksmuseum_SK-A-1377.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">Bombardment of Algiers</a> by the Anglo-Dutch fleet, to support the ultimatum to release European slaves, August 1816
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In July 1627 two pirate ships from Algiers under the command of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> pirate <a href="/wiki/Jan_Janszoon" title="Jan Janszoon">Jan Janszoon</a> sailed as far as <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Abductions" title="Turkish Abductions">raiding and capturing slaves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Two weeks earlier another pirate ship from <a href="/wiki/Sale,_Morocco" class="mw-redirect" title="Sale, Morocco">Salé</a> in <a href="/wiki/Saadi_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Saadi dynasty">Morocco</a> had also raided in Iceland. Some of the slaves brought to Algiers were later ransomed back to Iceland, but some chose to stay in Algeria. In 1629 pirate ships from Algeria raided the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Barbary raids in the Mediterranean continued to attack Spanish merchant shipping, and as a result, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Navy" title="Spanish Navy">Spanish Navy</a> bombarded Algiers in <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1783)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1783)">1783</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1784)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1784)">1784</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mikaberidze_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mikaberidze-35">[34]</a></sup> For the attack in 1784, the Spanish fleet was to be joined by ships from such traditional enemies of Algiers as <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Naples" title="Kingdom of Naples">Naples</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">Portugal</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Hospitaller" title="Knights Hospitaller">Knights of Malta</a>. Over 20,000 cannonballs were fired, much of the city and its fortifications were destroyed and most of the Algerian fleet was sunk.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 19th century, the pirates forged affiliations with Caribbean powers, paying a "licence tax" in exchange for safe harbour of their vessels.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Piracy on American vessels in the Mediterranean resulted in the United States initiating the <a href="/wiki/First_Barbary_War" title="First Barbary War">First</a> (1801–1805) and <a href="/wiki/Second_Barbary_War" title="Second Barbary War">Second Barbary Wars</a> (1815). Following those wars, Algeria was weaker and Europeans, with an Anglo-Dutch fleet commanded by the British <a href="/wiki/Edward_Pellew,_1st_Viscount_Exmouth" title="Edward Pellew, 1st Viscount Exmouth">Lord Exmouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bombardment_of_Algiers_(1816)" title="Bombardment of Algiers (1816)">attacked Algiers</a>. After a nine-hour bombardment, they obtained a treaty from the Dey that reaffirmed the conditions imposed by Captain (later Commodore) <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Decatur" title="Stephen Decatur">Stephen Decatur</a> (U.S. Navy) concerning the demands of tributes. In addition, the Dey agreed to end the practice of enslaving <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite being removed from Algeria in the 19th century, Spain retained a presence in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. Algeria consistently opposed Spanish fortresses and control in nearby Morocco through the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Mikaberidze_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mikaberidze-35">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="French_colonization_.281830.E2.80.931962.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonization_(1830–1962)">French colonization (1830–1962)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: French colonization (1830–1962)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/French_Algeria" title="French Algeria">French Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">Algerian War</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/French_North_Africa" title="French North Africa">French North Africa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/220px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="207" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/330px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg/440px-Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="702" data-file-height="662"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Vernet-Combat_de_Somah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Battle of Somah in 1836
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Under the pretext of a slight to their consul, the French invaded and <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Algiers_in_1830" title="Invasion of Algiers in 1830">captured Algiers</a> in 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Ben_Kiernan" title="Ben Kiernan">Ben Kiernan</a> wrote on the French conquest of Algeria: "By 1875, the French conquest was complete. The war had killed approximately 825,000 indigenous Algerians since 1830."<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> French losses from 1831 to 1851 were 92,329 dead in the hospital and only 3,336 killed in action.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> The population of Algeria, which stood at about 2.9 million in 1872, reached nearly 11 million in 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> French policy was predicated on "civilizing" the country.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> The slave trade and piracy in Algeria ceased following the French conquest.<sup id="cite_ref-Hannay_1911_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hannay_1911-37">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/French_conquest_of_Algeria" title="French conquest of Algeria">conquest of Algeria</a> by the French took some time and resulted in considerable bloodshed. A combination of violence and disease epidemics caused the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> Algerian population to decline by nearly one-third from 1830 to 1872.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ricoux1880_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ricoux1880-60">[59]</a></sup> On September 17, 1860, Napoleon III declared "Our first duty is to take care of the happiness of the three million Arabs, whom the fate of arms has brought under our domination. "<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> During this time, only Kabylia resisted, the Kabylians were not colonized until after the <a href="/wiki/Mokrani_Revolt" title="Mokrani Revolt">Mokrani revolt</a> in 1871. </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abd_al-Qadir.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Abd_al-Qadir.jpg/150px-Abd_al-Qadir.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="185" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Abd_al-Qadir.jpg/225px-Abd_al-Qadir.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Abd_al-Qadir.jpg/300px-Abd_al-Qadir.jpg 2x" data-file-width="392" data-file-height="483"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abd_al-Qadir.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Abdelkader_El_Djezairi" class="mw-redirect" title="Abdelkader El Djezairi">Emir Abdelkader</a>, Algerian leader insurgent against French colonial rule, 1865
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>From 1848 until independence, France administered the whole Mediterranean region of Algeria as an integral part and <i>département</i> of the nation. One of France's longest-held overseas territories, Algeria became a destination for hundreds of thousands of <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> <a href="/wiki/Immigrants" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrants">immigrants</a>, who became known as <i>colons</i> and later, as <i><a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pied-Noirs</a>.</i> Between 1825 and 1847, 50,000 French people emigrated to Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> These settlers benefited from the French government's confiscation of communal land from tribal peoples, and the application of modern agricultural techniques that increased the amount of arable land.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> Many Europeans settled in <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, and by the early 20th century they formed a majority of the population in both cities.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg/220px-Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="301" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg/330px-Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg/440px-Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="684"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Six_chefs_FLN_-_1954.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The six historical Leaders of the FLN: <a href="/wiki/Rabah_Bitat" title="Rabah Bitat">Rabah Bitat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mustapha_Benboula%C3%AFd" class="mw-redirect" title="Mustapha Benboulaïd">Mostefa Ben Boulaïd</a>, <a href="/wiki/Didouche_Mourad" title="Didouche Mourad">Didouche Mourad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Boudiaf" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohammed Boudiaf">Mohammed Boudiaf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krim_Belkacem" title="Krim Belkacem">Krim Belkacem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Larbi_Ben_M%27Hidi" class="mw-redirect" title="Larbi Ben M'Hidi">Larbi Ben M'Hidi</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During the late 19th and early 20th century; the <a href="/wiki/White_Africans_of_European_ancestry" title="White Africans of European ancestry">European share</a> was almost a fifth of the population. The French government aimed at making Algeria an assimilated part of France, and this included substantial educational investments especially after 1900. The indigenous cultural and religious resistance heavily opposed this tendency, but in contrast to the other colonised countries' path in central Asia and Caucasus, Algeria kept its individual skills and a relatively human-capital intensive agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 3 July 1940, the British <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> attacked the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a>'s fleet at <a href="/wiki/Mers_El_K%C3%A9bir" title="Mers El Kébir">Mers El Kébir</a>, killing nearly 1,300 men, with the goal of preventing the French warships from falling into German hands.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup> On 8 November 1942, Allied forces launched <a href="/wiki/Operation_Torch" title="Operation Torch">Operation Torch</a> landing in various places across <a href="/wiki/French_North_Africa" title="French North Africa">French North Africa</a>. </p>
      <p>Gradually, dissatisfaction among the Muslim population, which lacked political and economic status in the colonial system, gave rise to demands for greater political autonomy and eventually independence from France. In May 1945, the uprising against the occupying French forces was suppressed through what is now known as the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9tif_and_Guelma_massacre" title="Sétif and Guelma massacre">Sétif and Guelma massacre</a>. Tensions between the two population groups came to a head in 1954, when the first violent events of what was later called the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_War" title="Algerian War">Algerian War</a> began. Historians have estimated that between 30,000 and 150,000 <a href="/wiki/Harki" title="Harki">Harkis</a> and their dependants were killed by the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Front (Algeria)">Front de Libération Nationale</a> (FLN) or by <a href="/wiki/Lynching" title="Lynching">lynch</a> mobs in Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> The FLN used hit and run attacks in Algeria and France as part of its war, and the French conducted <a href="/wiki/Torture_during_the_Algerian_War_of_Independence" title="Torture during the Algerian War of Independence">severe reprisals</a>. </p>
      <p>The war led to the death of hundreds of thousands of Algerians and hundreds of thousands of injuries. Historians, like <a href="/wiki/Alistair_Horne" title="Alistair Horne">Alistair Horne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Aron" title="Raymond Aron">Raymond Aron</a>, state that the actual number of Algerian Muslim war dead was far greater than the original FLN and official French estimates but was less than the 1&nbsp;million deaths claimed by the Algerian government after independence. Horne estimated Algerian casualties during the span of eight years to be around 700,000.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> The war uprooted more than 2&nbsp;million Algerians.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The war against French rule concluded in 1962, when Algeria gained complete independence following the March 1962 <a href="/wiki/Evian_agreements" class="mw-redirect" title="Evian agreements">Evian agreements</a> and the July 1962 <a href="/wiki/Algerian_self-determination_referendum,_1962" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian self-determination referendum, 1962">self-determination referendum</a>. Some estimates put the Algerian death toll during the French colonial rule at over 10 million.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="The_first_three_decades_of_independence_.281962.E2.80.931991.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_first_three_decades_of_independence_(1962–1991)">The first three decades of independence (1962–1991)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The first three decades of independence (1962–1991)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Algeria_(1962%E2%80%9399)" title="History of Algeria (1962–99)">History of Algeria (1962–99)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The number of European <i><a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pied-Noirs</a></i> who fled Algeria totaled more than 900,000 between 1962 and 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup> The exodus to mainland France accelerated after the <a href="/wiki/Oran_massacre_of_1962" title="Oran massacre of 1962">Oran massacre of 1962</a>, in which hundreds of militants entered European sections of the city, and began attacking civilians. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg/150px-Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg/225px-Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg/300px-Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg 2x" data-file-width="414" data-file-height="550"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Houari_Boumediene%27s_Portrait.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Houari_Boumediene" class="mw-redirect" title="Houari Boumediene">Houari Boumediene</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Algeria's first president was the Front de Libération Nationale (<a href="/wiki/FLN_(Algeria)" class="mw-redirect" title="FLN (Algeria)">FLN</a>) leader <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Ben_Bella" title="Ahmed Ben Bella">Ahmed Ben Bella</a>. Morocco's claim to <a href="/wiki/Greater_Morocco" title="Greater Morocco">portions of western Algeria</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Sand_War" title="Sand War">Sand War</a> in 1963. Ben Bella was <a href="/wiki/1965_Algerian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1965 Algerian coup d'état">overthrown in 1965</a> by <a href="/wiki/Houari_Boum%C3%A9di%C3%A8ne" title="Houari Boumédiène">Houari Boumédiène</a>, his former ally and defence minister. Under Ben Bella, the government had become increasingly socialist and <a href="/wiki/Authoritarianism" title="Authoritarianism">authoritarian</a>; Boumédienne continued this trend. But, he relied much more on the army for his support, and reduced the sole legal party to a symbolic role. He <a href="/wiki/Collective_farming" title="Collective farming">collectivised</a> agriculture and launched a massive industrialisation drive. <a href="/wiki/Extraction_of_petroleum" title="Extraction of petroleum">Oil extraction</a> facilities were nationalised. This was especially beneficial to the leadership after the international <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>. </p>
      <p>In the 1960s and 1970s under President Houari Boumediene, Algeria pursued a program of industrialisation within a state-controlled socialist economy. Boumediene's successor, <a href="/wiki/Chadli_Bendjedid" title="Chadli Bendjedid">Chadli Bendjedid</a>, introduced some liberal economic reforms. He promoted a policy of <a href="/wiki/Arabisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabisation">Arabisation</a> in Algerian society and public life. Teachers of Arabic, brought in from other Muslim countries, spread conventional Islamic thought in schools and sowed the seeds of a return to Orthodox Islam.<sup id="cite_ref-faco_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faco-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Algerian economy became increasingly dependent on oil, leading to hardship when the price collapsed during the <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">1980s oil glut</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-74">[73]</a></sup> Economic recession caused by the crash in world oil prices resulted in Algerian social unrest during the 1980s; by the end of the decade, Bendjedid introduced a multi-party system. Political parties developed, such as the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Salvation_Front" title="Islamic Salvation Front">Islamic Salvation Front</a> (FIS), a broad coalition of Muslim groups.<sup id="cite_ref-faco_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faco-73">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Civil_War_.281991.E2.80.932002.29_and_aftermath"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_War_(1991–2002)_and_aftermath">Civil War (1991–2002) and aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Civil War (1991–2002) and aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Civil_War" title="Algerian Civil War">Algerian Civil War</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png/220px-Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png/330px-Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png/440px-Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="454"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Algerian_massacres_1997-1998.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/List_of_massacres_during_the_Algerian_Civil_War" title="List of massacres during the Algerian Civil War">Massacres</a> of over 50 people in 1997–1998. The <a href="/wiki/Armed_Islamic_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Armed Islamic Group">Armed Islamic Group (GIA)</a> claimed responsibility for many of them.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In December 1991 the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Salvation_Front" title="Islamic Salvation Front">Islamic Salvation Front</a> dominated the first of two rounds of <a href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_1991" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian legislative election, 1991">legislative elections</a>. Fearing the election of an Islamist government, the authorities intervened on 11 January 1992, cancelling the elections.
