Bendjedid resigned and a <a href="/wiki/High_Council_of_State_(Algeria)" title="High Council of State (Algeria)">High Council of State</a> was installed to act as the Presidency. It banned the FIS, triggering a civil <a href="/wiki/Insurgency" title="Insurgency">insurgency</a> between the Front's armed wing, the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Islamic_Group_of_Algeria" title="Armed Islamic Group of Algeria">Armed Islamic Group</a>, and the national armed forces, in which more than 100,000 people are thought to have died. The Islamist militants conducted a violent campaign of <a href="/wiki/List_of_massacres_during_the_Algerian_Civil_War" title="List of massacres during the Algerian Civil War">civilian massacres</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> At several points in the conflict, the situation in Algeria became a point of international concern, most notably during the crisis surrounding <a href="/wiki/Air_France_Flight_8969" title="Air France Flight 8969">Air France Flight 8969</a>, a hijacking perpetrated by the Armed Islamic Group. The Armed Islamic Group declared a ceasefire in October 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-faco_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faco-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Algeria held <a href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_1999" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian presidential election, 1999">elections in 1999</a>, considered biased by international observers and most opposition groups<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> which were won by President <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a>. He worked to restore political stability to the country and announced a "Civil Concord" initiative, approved in a <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Civil_Concord_referendum,_1999" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian Civil Concord referendum, 1999">referendum</a>, under which many political prisoners were pardoned, and several thousand members of armed groups were granted exemption from prosecution under a limited amnesty, in force until 13 January 2000. The AIS disbanded and levels of insurgent violence fell rapidly. The <a href="/wiki/Groupe_Salafiste_pour_la_Pr%C3%A9dication_et_le_Combat" class="mw-redirect" title="Groupe Salafiste pour la Prédication et le Combat">Groupe Salafiste pour la Prédication et le Combat</a> (GSPC), a splinter group of the Armed Islamic Group, continued a terrorist campaign against the Government.<sup id="cite_ref-faco_73-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faco-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bouteflika was re-elected in the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian presidential election, 2004">April 2004 presidential election</a> after campaigning on a programme of national reconciliation. The programme comprised economic, institutional, political and social reform to modernise the country, raise living standards, and tackle the causes of alienation. It also included a second amnesty initiative, the <a href="/wiki/Charter_for_Peace_and_National_Reconciliation" title="Charter for Peace and National Reconciliation">Charter for Peace and National Reconciliation</a>, which was approved in a <a href="/wiki/Algerian_national_reconciliation_referendum,_2005" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian national reconciliation referendum, 2005">referendum in September 2005</a>. It offered amnesty to most guerrillas and Government security forces.<sup id="cite_ref-faco_73-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faco-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian Constitution">Algerian Constitution</a> was amended following a vote in Parliament, removing the two-term limit on Presidential incumbents. This change enabled Bouteflika to stand for re-election in the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian presidential election, 2009">2009 presidential elections</a>, and he was re-elected in April 2009. During his election campaign and following his re-election, Bouteflika promised to extend the programme of national reconciliation and a $150-billion spending programme to create three million new jobs, the construction of one million new housing units, and to continue public sector and infrastructure modernisation programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-faco_73-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faco-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A continuing series of protests throughout the country started on 28 December 2010, inspired by similar <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">protests across the Middle East and North Africa</a>. On 24 February 2011, the government lifted Algeria's 19-year-old <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> The government enacted legislation dealing with political parties, the electoral code, and the representation of women in elected bodies.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> In April 2011, Bouteflika promised further constitutional and political reform.<sup id="cite_ref-faco_73-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faco-73">[72]</a></sup> However, elections are routinely criticized by opposition groups as unfair and international human rights groups say that media censorship and harassment of political opponents continue. </p>
      <p>On 2 April 2019, Bouteflika resigned from the presidency after <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Algerian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2019–2020 Algerian protests">mass protests</a> against his candidacy for a fifth term in office.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Algeria" title="Geography of Algeria">Geography of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria_relief.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/220px-Algeria_relief.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/330px-Algeria_relief.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Algeria_relief.png/440px-Algeria_relief.png 2x" data-file-width="624" data-file-height="532"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria_relief.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hoggar_Mountains" title="Hoggar Mountains">Hoggar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Mountains" title="Atlas Mountains">Atlas mountains</a> compose the Algerian relief.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dunes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Dunes.jpg/220px-Dunes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Dunes.jpg/330px-Dunes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/35/Dunes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="300"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dunes.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Desert" title="Algerian Desert">Algerian Desert</a> makes up more than 90% of the country's total area
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the 2011 breakup of <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, Algeria has been the largest country in Africa, and the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>. Its southern part includes a significant portion of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. To the north, the <a href="/wiki/Tell_Atlas" title="Tell Atlas">Tell Atlas</a> form with the <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Atlas" title="Saharan Atlas">Saharan Atlas</a>, further south, two parallel sets of reliefs in approaching eastbound, and between which are inserted vast plains and highlands. Both Atlas tend to merge in eastern Algeria. The vast mountain ranges of <a href="/wiki/Aures" class="mw-redirect" title="Aures">Aures</a> and <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A9bessa" title="Tébessa">Nememcha</a> occupy the entire northeastern Algeria and are delineated by the Tunisian border. The highest point is <a href="/wiki/Mount_Tahat" title="Mount Tahat">Mount Tahat</a> (3,003 metres or 9,852 feet). </p>
      <p>Algeria lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/19th_parallel_north" title="19th parallel north">19°</a> and <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">37°N</a> (a small area is north of 37°N and south of 19°N), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/9th_meridian_west" title="9th meridian west">9°W</a> and <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°E</a>. Most of the coastal area is hilly, sometimes even mountainous, and there are a few natural <a href="/wiki/Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Harbour">harbours</a>. The area from the coast to the Tell Atlas is fertile. South of the Tell Atlas is a <a href="/wiki/Steppe" title="Steppe">steppe</a> landscape ending with the <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Atlas" title="Saharan Atlas">Saharan Atlas</a>; farther south, there is the Sahara desert.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-80">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Hoggar_Mountains" title="Hoggar Mountains">Hoggar Mountains</a> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">جبال هقار</span>‎), also known as the Hoggar, are a highland region in central Sahara, southern Algeria. They are located about 1,500&nbsp;km (932&nbsp;mi) south of the capital, Algiers, and just east of <a href="/wiki/Tamanghasset" class="mw-redirect" title="Tamanghasset">Tamanghasset</a>. Algiers, <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Algeria" title="Constantine, Algeria">Constantine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> are Algeria's main cities.<sup id="cite_ref-LOC_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LOC-80">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_and_hydrology">Climate and hydrology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate and hydrology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Algeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Climate of Algeria">Climate of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg/300px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg/450px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg/600px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1391" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_DZA_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Algeria map of Köppen climate classification.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg/220px-From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg/330px-From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg/440px-From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="472"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:From_tikejda_Algeria_by_%C3%BB%C3%B8k%C3%AFh%C3%A7t.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Tikjda" title="Tikjda">Tikjda</a> ski resort in northern Algeria
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In this region, midday desert temperatures can be hot year round. After sunset, however, the clear, dry air permits rapid loss of heat, and the nights are cool to chilly. Enormous daily ranges in temperature are recorded. </p>
      <p>Rainfall is fairly plentiful along the coastal part of the Tell Atlas, ranging from 400 to 670&nbsp;mm (15.7 to 26.4&nbsp;in) annually, the amount of precipitation increasing from west to east. <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> is heaviest in the northern part of eastern Algeria, where it reaches as much as 1,000&nbsp;mm (39.4&nbsp;in) in some years. </p>
      <p>Farther inland, the rainfall is less plentiful. Algeria also has <a href="/wiki/Erg_(landform)" title="Erg (landform)">ergs</a>, or sand dunes, between mountains. Among these, in the summer time when winds are heavy and gusty, temperatures can go up to 43.3&nbsp;°C (110&nbsp;°F). </p> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="excerpt"> 
        <p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Algeria" title="Climate change in Algeria">Climate change in Algeria </a> has wide reaching effects on the country. Algeria was not a significant contributor to climate change,<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al-81">[80]</a></sup> but like <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Middle_East_and_North_Africa" title="Climate change in the Middle East and North Africa">other countries in the Mena region</a>, is expected to be on the front-lines of climate change impacts.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:1_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:1-82">[81]</a></sup> </p>
        <p>Because a large part of the <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Algeria" title="Geography of Algeria">country is in already hot and arid geographies</a>, including part of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, already strong heat and <a href="/wiki/Water_resource" class="mw-redirect" title="Water resource">water resource</a> access challenges are expected to get worse.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al-81">[80]</a></sup> As early as 2014, <a href="/wiki/Scientists" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientists">scientists</a> were attributing extreme heat waves to climate change in Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:0al-81">[80]</a></sup> </p> Algeria was ranked 46th of countries in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Climate_Change_Performance_Index" title="Climate Change Performance Index">Climate Change Performance Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:2_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Algeria_:2-83">[82]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna_and_flora">Fauna and flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fauna and flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Algeria" title="Wildlife of Algeria">Wildlife of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_(Algeria).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg/220px-C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg/330px-C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg/440px-C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_%28Algeria%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A8dre_du_Ch%C3%A9lia_13_(Algeria).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">Cedrus</a> of Chélia in the <a href="/wiki/Aures" class="mw-redirect" title="Aures">Aures</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg/220px-Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg/330px-Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg/440px-Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1152"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nature_in_algeria_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Algeria varies from coastal areas to mountainous areas and deserts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The varied vegetation of Algeria includes <a href="/wiki/Coastal" class="mw-redirect" title="Coastal">coastal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountainous" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountainous">mountainous</a> and grassy <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>-like regions which all support a wide range of wildlife. Many of the creatures comprising the Algerian wildlife live in close proximity to civilisation. The most commonly seen animals include the wild <a href="/wiki/Boar" class="mw-redirect" title="Boar">boars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackal" title="Jackal">jackals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gazelle" title="Gazelle">gazelles</a>, although it is not uncommon to spot <a href="/wiki/Fennecs" class="mw-redirect" title="Fennecs">fennecs</a> (foxes), and <a href="/wiki/Jerboas" class="mw-redirect" title="Jerboas">jerboas</a>. Algeria also has a small <a href="/wiki/African_leopard" title="African leopard">African leopard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saharan_cheetah" class="mw-redirect" title="Saharan cheetah">Saharan cheetah</a> population, but these are seldom seen. A species of deer, the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_stag" title="Barbary stag">Barbary stag</a>, inhabits the dense humid forests in the north-eastern areas. </p>
      <p>A variety of bird species makes the country an attraction for bird watchers. The forests are inhabited by boars and jackals. <a href="/wiki/Barbary_macaque" title="Barbary macaque">Barbary macaques</a> are the sole native monkey. Snakes, <a href="/wiki/Monitor_lizard" title="Monitor lizard">monitor lizards</a>, and numerous other reptiles can be found living among an array of <a href="/wiki/Rodent" title="Rodent">rodents</a> throughout the <a href="/wiki/Semi_arid" class="mw-redirect" title="Semi arid">semi arid</a> regions of Algeria. Many animals are now extinct, including the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_lion" title="Barbary lion">Barbary lions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Atlas_bear" title="Atlas bear">Atlas bears</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_African_crocodile" title="West African crocodile">crocodiles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the north, some of the native flora includes <a href="/wiki/Macchia" class="mw-redirect" title="Macchia">Macchia</a> scrub, <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olive trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oaks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cedrus" title="Cedrus">cedars</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Pinophyta" title="Pinophyta">conifers</a>. The mountain regions contain large forests of evergreens (<a href="/wiki/Aleppo_pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Aleppo pine">Aleppo pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juniper" title="Juniper">juniper</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Evergreen_oak" class="mw-redirect" title="Evergreen oak">evergreen oak</a>) and some deciduous trees. <a href="/wiki/Ficus" title="Ficus">Fig</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eucalyptus" title="Eucalyptus">eucalyptus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agave" title="Agave">agave</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">palm trees</a> grow in the warmer areas. The <a href="/wiki/Grape_vine" class="mw-redirect" title="Grape vine">grape vine</a> is indigenous to the coast. In the Sahara region, some oases have palm trees. <a href="/wiki/Acacia" title="Acacia">Acacias</a> with wild <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">olives</a> are the predominant flora in the remainder of the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>. Algeria had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 5.22/10, ranking it 106th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-85">[84]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Camel" title="Camel">Camels</a> are used extensively; the desert also abounds with venomous and nonvenomous snakes, <a href="/wiki/Scorpion" title="Scorpion">scorpions</a>, and numerous insects. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Algeria" title="Politics of Algeria">Politics of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg/150px-Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ed/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="190" data-file-height="303"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abdelmadjid_Tebboune_20200119.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Abdelmadjid_Tebboune" title="Abdelmadjid Tebboune">Abdelmadjid Tebboune</a>, President of Algeria since 2019
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Elected politicians have relatively little sway over Algeria. Instead, a group of unelected civilian and military "décideurs" ("deciders"), known as "le pouvoir" ("the power"), actually rule the country, even deciding who should be president.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The most powerful man might have been <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Medi%C3%A8ne" title="Mohamed Mediène">Mohamed Mediène</a>, the head of military intelligence, before he was brought down during the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Algerian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2019–2020 Algerian protests">2019 protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> In recent years, many of these generals have died, retired, or been imprisoned. After the death of General <a href="/wiki/Larbi_Belkheir" title="Larbi Belkheir">Larbi Belkheir</a>, Previous president <a href="/wiki/Bouteflika" title="Bouteflika">Bouteflika</a> put loyalists in key posts, notably at <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, and secured constitutional amendments that made him re-electable indefinitely, until he was brought down in 2019 during <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%932020_Algerian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2019–2020 Algerian protests">protests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The head of state is the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Algeria" title="President of Algeria">President of Algeria</a>, who is elected for a five-year term. The president was formerly limited to two five-year terms, but a constitutional amendment passed by the Parliament on 11 November 2008 removed this limitation.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2019_Algerian_presidential_election" title="2019 Algerian presidential election">next presidential election</a> was planned to be in April 2019, but <a href="/wiki/2019_Algerian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 Algerian protests">widespread protests</a> erupted on 22 February against the president's decision to participate in the election, which resulted in President Bouteflika announcing his resignation on 3 April.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> Algeria has universal <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> at 18 years of age.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-3">[3]</a></sup> The President is the head of the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian Army">army</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Ministers_of_Algeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Ministers of Algeria">Council of Ministers</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=High_Security_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="High Security Council (page does not exist)">High Security Council</a>. He appoints the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Algeria" title="Prime Minister of Algeria">Prime Minister</a> who is also the head of government.<sup id="cite_ref-president_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-president-90">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_(Alg%C3%A9rie).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/220px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/330px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg/440px-H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_%28Alg%C3%A9rie%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4080" data-file-height="2720"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:H%C3%A9micycle_de_l%27assembl%C3%A9e_populaire_nationale_(Alg%C3%A9rie).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Assembly" title="People's National Assembly">People's National Assembly</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Algerian parliament is <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a>; the lower house, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Assembly" title="People's National Assembly">People's National Assembly</a>, has 462 members who are directly elected for five-year terms, while the upper house, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Nation" title="Council of the Nation">Council of the Nation</a>, has 144 members serving six-year terms, of which 96 members are chosen by local assemblies and 48 are appointed by the president.<sup id="cite_ref-fitw13_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fitw13-91">[90]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Algeria" title="Constitution of Algeria">constitution</a>, no political association may be formed if it is "based on differences in religion, language, race, gender, profession, or region". In addition, political campaigns must be exempt from the aforementioned subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Parliamentary elections were last held in <a href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_2012" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian legislative election, 2012">May 2012</a>, and were judged to be largely free by international monitors, though local groups alleged fraud and irregularities.<sup id="cite_ref-fitw13_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fitw13-91">[90]</a></sup> In the elections, the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Front_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Front (Algeria)">FLN</a> won 221 seats, the military-backed <a href="/wiki/National_Rally_for_Democracy_(Algeria)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Rally for Democracy (Algeria)">National Rally for Democracy</a> won 70, and the Islamist <a href="/wiki/Green_Algeria_Alliance" title="Green Algeria Alliance">Green Algeria Alliance</a> won 47.<sup id="cite_ref-fitw13_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fitw13-91">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Algeria" title="Foreign relations of Algeria">Foreign relations of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/220px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/330px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg/440px-Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Abdelaziz_Bouteflika_and_George_W_Bush_20080707.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>President <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a> and <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> exchange handshakes at the Windsor Hotel Toya Resort and Spa in Tōyako Town, Abuta District, Hokkaidō in 2008. With them are <a href="/wiki/Dmitriy_Medvedev" class="mw-redirect" title="Dmitriy Medvedev">Dmitriy Medvedev</a>, left, and <a href="/wiki/Yasuo_Fukuda" title="Yasuo Fukuda">Yasuo Fukuda</a>, right.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Algeria is included in the European Union's <a href="/wiki/European_Neighbourhood_Policy" title="European Neighbourhood Policy">European Neighbourhood Policy</a> (ENP) which aims at bringing the EU and its neighbours closer. Giving incentives and rewarding best performers, as well as offering funds in a faster and more flexible manner, are the two main principles underlying the European Neighbourhood Instrument (ENI) that came into force in 2014. It has a budget of €15.4 billion and provides the bulk of funding through a number of programmes. </p>
      <p>In 2009, the French government agreed to compensate victims of nuclear tests in Algeria. Defense Minister Herve Morin stated that "It's time for our country to be at peace with itself, at peace thanks to a system of compensation and reparations," when presenting the draft law on the payouts. Algerian officials and activists believe that this is a good first step and hope that this move would encourage broader reparation.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tensions between Algeria and Morocco in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Western_Sahara" title="Western Sahara">Western Sahara</a> have been an obstacle to tightening the <a href="/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union" title="Arab Maghreb Union">Arab Maghreb Union</a>, nominally established in 1989, but which has carried little practical weight.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Algeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Algeria">Military of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The military of Algeria consists of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="People's National Army">People's National Army</a> (ANP), the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_National_Navy" title="Algerian National Navy">Algerian National Navy</a> (MRA), and the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Air_Force" title="Algerian Air Force">Algerian Air Force</a> (QJJ), plus the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Air_Defence_Forces" title="Territorial Air Defence Forces">Territorial Air Defence Forces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> It is the direct successor of the <a href="/wiki/National_Liberation_Army_(Algeria)" title="National Liberation Army (Algeria)">National Liberation Army</a> (Armée de Libération Nationale or ALN), the armed wing of the nationalist National Liberation Front which fought French colonial <a href="/wiki/Military_occupation" title="Military occupation">occupation</a> during the Algerian War of Independence (1954–62). </p>
      <p>Total military personnel include 147,000 active, 150,000 reserve, and 187,000 paramilitary staff (2008 estimate).<sup id="cite_ref-IISS_TMB_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IISS_TMB-96">[95]</a></sup> Service in the military is compulsory for men aged 19–30, for a total of 12 months.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> The military expenditure was 4.3% of the <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> (GDP) in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> Algeria has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel" title="List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel">second largest military</a> in North Africa with the largest defence budget in Africa ($10 billion).<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaSpending_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaSpending-98">[97]</a></sup> Most of Algeria's weapons are imported from <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, with whom they are a close ally.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaSpending_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaSpending-98">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2007, the Algerian Air Force signed a deal with Russia to purchase 49 <a href="/wiki/MiG-29" class="mw-redirect" title="MiG-29">MiG-29</a>SMT and 6 MiG-29UBT at an estimated cost of $1.9&nbsp;billion. Russia is also building two <a href="/wiki/Kilo_class_submarine" class="mw-redirect" title="Kilo class submarine">636-type</a> diesel <a href="/wiki/Submarines" class="mw-redirect" title="Submarines">submarines</a> for Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Algeria" title="Human rights in Algeria">Human rights in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Algeria has been categorized by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> as "not free" since it began publishing such ratings in 1972, with the exception of 1989, 1990, and 1991, when the country was labeled "partly free."<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> In December 2016, the <i>Euro-Mediterranean Human Rights Monitor</i> issued a report regarding violation of <a href="/wiki/Media_freedom" class="mw-redirect" title="Media freedom">media freedom</a> in Algeria. It clarified that the Algerian government imposed restriction on <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">freedom of the press</a>; expression; and right to peaceful demonstration, protest and assembly as well as intensified censorship of the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_media" class="mw-redirect" title="Broadcast media">media</a> and websites. Due to the fact that the journalists and activists criticize the ruling government, some media organizations' licenses are cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Independent and autonomous trade unions face routine harassment from the government, with many leaders imprisoned and protests suppressed. In 2016 a number of unions, many of which were involved in the 2010–2012 Algerian Protests, have been deregistered by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Algeria" title="LGBT rights in Algeria">Homosexuality</a> is illegal in Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> Public homosexual behavior is punishable by up to two years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a> has accused the Algerian authorities of using the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> as an excuse to prevent pro-democracy movements and protests in the country, leading to the arrest of youths as part of <a href="/wiki/Social_distancing" title="Social distancing">social distancing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">Provinces of Algeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Algeria" title="Districts of Algeria">Districts of Algeria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Algeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of Algeria">Municipalities of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Algeria is divided into 58 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">provinces</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Wilaya" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilaya">wilayas</a></i>), 553 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Algeria" title="Districts of Algeria">districts</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Da%C3%AFra" title="Daïra">daïras</a></i>) and 1,541 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Algeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Municipalities of Algeria">municipalities</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Baladiyah" title="Baladiyah">baladiyahs</a></i>). Each province, district, and municipality is named after its <a href="/wiki/Capital_city" title="Capital city">seat</a>, which is usually the largest city. </p>
      <p>The administrative divisions have changed several times since independence. When introducing new provinces, the numbers of old provinces are kept, hence the non-alphabetical order. With their official numbers, currently (since 1983) they are<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left;font-size:80%;margin:1em auto;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>#</th> 
         <th><a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">Wilaya</a></th> 
         <th>Area (km<sup>2</sup>)</th> 
         <th>Population</th> 
         <th>map</th> 
         <th>#</th> 
         <th><a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Algeria" title="Provinces of Algeria">Wilaya</a></th> 
         <th>Area (km<sup>2</sup>)</th> 
         <th>Population </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td>1</td> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Adrar_Province" title="Adrar Province">Adrar</a></td> 
         <td style="text-align:right">402,197</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right">439,700 </td> 
         <td rowspan="57">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Algeria" title="Economy of Algeria">Economy of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg/250px-Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg/375px-Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg/500px-Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1102" data-file-height="863"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria_Export_Treemap.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of the country's exports in 28 colour-coded categories.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Algeria is classified as an upper middle income country by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> Algeria's currency is the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_dinar" title="Algerian dinar">dinar</a> (DZD). The economy remains dominated by the state, a legacy of the country's socialist post-independence development model. In recent years, the Algerian government has halted the privatization of state-owned industries and imposed restrictions on imports and foreign involvement in its economy.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> These restrictions are just starting to be lifted off recently although questions about Algeria's slowly-diversifying economy remain. </p>
      <p>Algeria has struggled to develop industries outside hydrocarbons in part because of high costs and an inert state bureaucracy. The government's efforts to diversify the economy by attracting foreign and domestic investment outside the energy sector have done little to reduce high youth unemployment rates or to address housing shortages.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> The country is facing a number of short-term and medium-term problems, including the need to diversify the economy, strengthen political, economic and financial reforms, improve the business climate and reduce inequalities amongst regions.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>A wave of economic protests in February and March 2011 prompted the Algerian government to offer more than $23 billion in public grants and retroactive salary and benefit increases. Public spending has increased by 27% annually during the past 5 years. The 2010–14 public-investment programme will cost US$286 billion, 40% of which will go to human development.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_d%27oran.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Theatre_d%27oran.jpg/220px-Theatre_d%27oran.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Theatre_d%27oran.jpg/330px-Theatre_d%27oran.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Theatre_d%27oran.jpg/440px-Theatre_d%27oran.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_d%27oran.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The port city of Oran
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Algerian economy grew by 2.6% in 2011, driven by public spending, in particular in the construction and public-works sector, and by growing internal demand. If hydrocarbons are excluded, growth has been estimated at 4.8%. Growth of 3% is expected in 2012, rising to 4.2% in 2013. The rate of inflation was 4% and the budget deficit 3% of GDP. The current-account surplus is estimated at 9.3% of GDP and at the end of December 2011, official reserves were put at US$182 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> Inflation, the lowest in the region, has remained stable at 4% on average between 2003 and 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-MFW4A_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MFW4A-110">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/250px-Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" decoding="async" width="250" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/375px-Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fe/Algeria%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 2x" data-file-width="442" data-file-height="272"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Algeria, trends in the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> 1970–2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2011 Algeria announced a budgetary surplus of $26.9 billion, 62% increase in comparison to 2010 surplus. In general, the country exported $73 billion worth of commodities while it imported $46 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Thanks to strong hydrocarbon revenues, Algeria has a cushion of $173 billion in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_currency_reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign currency reserves">foreign currency reserves</a> and a large hydrocarbon stabilization fund. In addition, Algeria's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_external_debt" title="List of countries by external debt">external debt</a> is extremely low at about 2% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> The economy remains very dependent on hydrocarbon wealth, and, despite high foreign exchange reserves (US$178 billion, equivalent to three years of imports), current expenditure growth makes Algeria's budget more vulnerable to the risk of prolonged lower hydrocarbon revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-imfart4_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-112">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2011, the agricultural sector and services recorded growth of 10% and 5.3%, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> About 14% of the labor force are employed in the <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Algeria" title="Agriculture in Algeria">agricultural sector</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> Fiscal policy in 2011 remained expansionist and made it possible to maintain the pace of public investment and to contain the strong demand for jobs and housing.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Algeria has not joined the <a href="/wiki/WTO" class="mw-redirect" title="WTO">WTO</a>, despite several years of negotiations.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2006, Russia agreed to erase $4.74&nbsp;billion of Algeria's <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet</a>-era debt<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> during a visit by <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a> to the country, the first by a Russian leader in half a century. In return, <a href="/wiki/President_of_Algeria" title="President of Algeria">Algerian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a> agreed to buy $7.5&nbsp;billion worth of combat planes, air-defence systems and other arms from Russia, according to the head of Russia's state arms exporter <a href="/wiki/Rosoboronexport" title="Rosoboronexport">Rosoboronexport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Dubai-based conglomerate Emarat Dzayer Group said it had signed a joint venture agreement to develop a $1.6 billion steel factory in Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_and_Natural_Resources">Oil and Natural Resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Oil and Natural Resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Algeria" title="Mining industry of Algeria">Mining industry of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/220px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/330px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg/440px-Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg 2x" data-file-width="832" data-file-height="799"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Algeria_pipelines_map.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Pipelines across Algeria
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Algeria, whose economy is reliant on petroleum, has been an <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">OPEC</a> member since 1969. Its crude oil production stands at around 1.1 million barrels/day, but it is also a major gas producer and exporter, with important links to Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-opb15_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opb15-118">[117]</a></sup> Hydrocarbons have long been the backbone of the economy, accounting for roughly 60% of budget revenues, 30% of GDP, and over 95% of export earnings. Algeria has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_proven_reserves" title="List of countries by natural gas proven reserves">10th-largest reserves of natural gas</a> in the world and is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_natural_gas_exports" title="List of countries by natural gas exports">sixth-largest gas exporter</a>. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a> reported that in 2005, Algeria had 4.5&nbsp;trillion cubic metres (160<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>12</sup>&nbsp;cu&nbsp;ft) of proven <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_reserves" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas reserves">natural-gas reserves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ciawfb_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ciawfb-119">[118]</a></sup> It also ranks <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_proven_oil_reserves" title="List of countries by proven oil reserves">16th in oil reserves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Non-hydrocarbon growth for 2011 was projected at 5%. To cope with social demands, the authorities raised expenditure, especially on basic food support, employment creation, support for SMEs, and higher salaries. High hydrocarbon prices have improved the current account and the already large international reserves position.<sup id="cite_ref-imfart4_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-112">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Income from oil and gas rose in 2011 as a result of continuing high oil prices, though the trend in production volume is downwards.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> Production from the oil and gas sector in terms of volume, continues to decline, dropping from 43.2 million tonnes to 32 million tonnes between 2007 and 2011. Nevertheless, the sector accounted for 98% of the total volume of exports in 2011, against 48% in 1962,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> and 70% of budgetary receipts, or US$71.4 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Algerian national oil company is <a href="/wiki/Sonatrach" title="Sonatrach">Sonatrach</a>, which plays a key role in all aspects of the oil and natural gas sectors in Algeria. All foreign operators must work in partnership with Sonatrach, which usually has majority ownership in production-sharing agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Algeria is lower than world average. In 2016, Algeria had 0.53 global hectares<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-122">[121]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much less than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> In 2016 Algeria used 2.4 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use just under 4.5 times as much biocapacity as Algeria contains. As a result, Algeria is running a biocapacity deficit.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_122-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-122">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_alternative_energy_sources">Research and alternative energy sources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Research and alternative energy sources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Algeria has invested an estimated 100 billion dinars towards developing research facilities and paying researchers. This development program is meant to advance alternative energy production, especially solar and wind power.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> Algeria is estimated to have the largest solar energy potential in the Mediterranean, so the government has funded the creation of a solar science park in Hassi R'Mel. Currently, Algeria has 20,000 research professors at various universities and over 780 research labs, with state-set goals to expand to 1,000. Besides solar energy, areas of research in Algeria include space and satellite telecommunications, nuclear power and medical research. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour_market">Labour market</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Labour market">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Despite a decline in total <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, youth and women unemployment is high.<sup id="cite_ref-imfart4_112-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfart4-112">[111]</a></sup> Unemployment particularly affects the young, with a jobless rate of 21.5% among the 15–24 age group.<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The overall rate of unemployment was 10% in 2011, but remained higher among young people, with a rate of 21.5% for those aged between 15 and 24. The government strengthened in 2011 the job programmes introduced in 1988, in particular in the framework of the programme to aid those seeking work (Dispositif d'Aide à l'Insertion Professionnelle).<sup id="cite_ref-aaeo_78-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaeo-78">[77]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Algeria" title="Tourism in Algeria">Tourism in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/220px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/330px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg/440px-Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4500" data-file-height="2981"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Giants_-_Rock_towers_in_the_Algerian_Sahara.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Djanet" title="Djanet">Djanet</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The development of the tourism sector in Algeria had previously been hampered by a lack of facilities, but since 2004 a broad tourism development strategy has been implemented resulting in many hotels of a high modern standard being built. </p>
      <p>There are several <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a> in Algeria<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Al_Qal%27a_of_Beni_Hammad" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Qal'a of Beni Hammad">Al Qal'a of Beni Hammad</a>, the first capital of the <a href="/wiki/Hammadid" class="mw-redirect" title="Hammadid">Hammadid</a> empire; <a href="/wiki/Tipasa" title="Tipasa">Tipasa</a>, a Phoenician and later Roman town; and <a href="/wiki/Dj%C3%A9mila" title="Djémila">Djémila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timgad" title="Timgad">Timgad</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Roman</a> ruins; <a href="/wiki/M%27Zab_Valley" class="mw-redirect" title="M'Zab Valley">M'Zab Valley</a>, a limestone valley containing a large urbanized <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oasis</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Casbah" class="mw-redirect" title="Casbah">Casbah</a> of Algiers, an important citadel. The only natural <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Tassili_n%27Ajjer" title="Tassili n'Ajjer">Tassili n'Ajjer</a>, a mountain range. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Algeria" title="Transport in Algeria">Transport in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/220px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/330px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG/440px-Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1528" data-file-height="808"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Autoroute_est_ouest_ghomri2.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The main highway connecting the Moroccan to the Tunisian border was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Cairo%E2%80%93Dakar_Highway" title="Cairo–Dakar Highway">Cairo–Dakar Highway</a> project
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Algerian road network is the densest in Africa; its length is estimated at 180,000&nbsp;km (110,000&nbsp;mi) of highways, with more than 3,756 structures and a paving rate of 85%. This network will be complemented by the <a href="/wiki/Algeria_East%E2%80%93West_Highway" title="Algeria East–West Highway">East-West Highway</a>, a major infrastructure project currently under construction. It is a 3-way, 1,216-kilometre-long (756&nbsp;mi) highway, linking <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> in the extreme east to the <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a> in the far west. Algeria is also crossed by the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Sahara_Highway" title="Trans-Sahara Highway">Trans-Sahara Highway</a>, which is now completely paved. This road is supported by the Algerian government to increase trade between the six countries crossed: Algeria, <a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Algeria" title="Demographics of Algeria">Demographics of Algeria</a>
