      <p>In January 2016 Algeria's population was an estimated 40.4&nbsp;million, who are mainly <a href="/wiki/Arab-Berber" title="Arab-Berber">Arab-Berber</a> ethnically.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ons_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ons-128">[127]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ber_evidance_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ber_evidance-129">[128]</a></sup> At the outset of the 20th century, its population was approximately four million.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> About 90% of Algerians live in the northern, coastal area; the inhabitants of the Sahara desert are mainly concentrated in <a href="/wiki/Oasis" title="Oasis">oases</a>, although some 1.5&nbsp;million remain <a href="/wiki/Nomad" title="Nomad">nomadic</a> or partly nomadic. 28.1% of Algerians are under the age of 15.<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Women make up 70% of the country's lawyers and 60% of its judges and also dominate the field of medicine. Increasingly, women are contributing more to household income than men. 60% of university students are women, according to university researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between 90,000 and 165,000 <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">Sahrawis</a> from Western Sahara live in the <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_refugee_camps" title="Sahrawi refugee camps">Sahrawi refugee camps</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRAlgeria_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRAlgeria-132">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USCRIAlgeria_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCRIAlgeria-133">[132]</a></sup> in the western Algerian Sahara desert.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> There are also more than 4,000 <a href="/wiki/Palestinian_refugee" class="mw-redirect" title="Palestinian refugee">Palestinian refugees</a>, who are well integrated and have not asked for assistance from the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).<sup id="cite_ref-UNHCRAlgeria_132-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNHCRAlgeria-132">[131]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USCRIAlgeria_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USCRIAlgeria-133">[132]</a></sup> In 2009, 35,000 <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> migrant workers lived in Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The largest concentration of Algerian migrants outside Algeria is in France, which has reportedly over 1.7 million Algerians of up to the second generation.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Algeria" title="Ethnic groups in Algeria">Ethnic groups in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Indigenous <a href="/wiki/Berbers" title="Berbers">Berbers</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Phoenicians" class="mw-redirect" title="Phoenicians">Phoenicians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Greeks" title="Byzantine Greeks">Byzantine Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab people">Arabs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a>, various <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africans" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-Saharan Africans">Sub-Saharan Africans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> have contributed to the history of Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> Descendants of <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Andalusian</a> refugees are also present in the population of Algiers and other cities.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> Moreover, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> was spoken by these <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragonese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castilian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Castilian people">Castillian</a> <a href="/wiki/Moriscos" class="mw-redirect" title="Moriscos">Morisco</a> descendants deep into the 18th century, and even <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> was spoken at the same time by <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalan</a> <a href="/wiki/Moriscos" class="mw-redirect" title="Moriscos">Morisco</a> descendants in the small town of Grish El-Oued.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/220px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/330px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png/440px-Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png 2x" data-file-width="454" data-file-height="263"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tenus_traditionnelles_alg%C3%A9riennes_27.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Some of Algeria's traditional clothes
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Despite the dominance of the Berber ethnicity in Algeria, the majority of Algerians identify with an Arabic-based identity, especially after the Arab nationalism rising in the 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> Berbers and Berber-speaking Algerians are divided into many groups with varying languages. The largest of these are the Kabyles, who live in the <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a> region east of Algiers, the Chaoui of Northeast Algeria, the Tuaregs in the southern desert and the <a href="/wiki/Chenouas" title="Chenouas">Shenwa people</a> of North Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="This citation requires a reference to the specific page or range of pages in which the material appears. (February 2013)">page&nbsp;needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>During the colonial period, there was a large (10% in 1960)<sup id="cite_ref-Cook_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cook-143">[142]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a> population who became known as <i><a href="/wiki/Pied-Noir" title="Pied-Noir">Pied-Noirs</a></i>. They were primarily of French, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish people">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian people">Italian</a> origin. Almost all of this population left during the war of independence or immediately after its end.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Algeria" title="Languages of Algeria">Languages of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/220px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/330px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg/440px-Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tizi_Ouzou_Tasdawit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Signs in the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tizi_Ouzou" title="University of Tizi Ouzou">University of Tizi Ouzou</a> in three languages: <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a>, and French
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berber_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber language">Berber</a> are the official languages.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a> (Darja) is the language used by the majority of the population. Colloquial Algerian Arabic is heavily infused with borrowings from French and Berber. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Berber_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Berber language">Berber</a> has been recognised as a "national language" by the constitutional amendment of 8 May 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kabyle_language" title="Kabyle language">Kabyle</a>, the predominant Berber language, is taught and is partially co-official (with a few restrictions) in parts of <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" class="mw-redirect" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a>. In February 2016, the Algerian constitution passed a resolution that would make Berber an official language alongside Arabic. </p>
      <p>Although <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> has no official status, Algeria is the second-largest Francophone country in the world in terms of speakers,<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> and French is widely used in government, media (newspapers, radio, local television), and both the education system (from primary school onwards) and academia due to <a href="/wiki/French_rule_in_Algeria" class="mw-redirect" title="French rule in Algeria">Algeria's colonial history</a>. It can be regarded as a <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a> of Algeria. In 2008, 11.2 million Algerians could read and write in French.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> An Abassa Institute study in April 2000 found that 60% of households could speak and understand French or 18 million in a population of 30 million then. After an earlier period during which the Algerian government tried to phase out French, in recent decades the government has backtracked and reinforced the study of French, and some television programs are broadcast in the language. </p>
      <p>Algeria emerged as a bilingual state after 1962.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> Colloquial <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Arabic" title="Algerian Arabic">Algerian Arabic</a> is spoken by about 72% of the population and Berber by 27–30%.<sup id="cite_ref-leclerc_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leclerc-150">[149]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Algeria" title="Religion in Algeria">Religion in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Early_African_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Early African Church">Early African Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Algeria" title="History of the Jews in Algeria">History of the Jews in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr style="background:#ddd">
           <th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Religion in Algeria, 2010 (<a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-pew_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-151">[150]</a></sup></th>
          </tr> 
          <tr style="font-size:88%; height:4px;"> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; text-align:left;">Religion</td> 
           <td style="width:100px; text-align:left;"></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding:0 4px; width:1em; text-align:right;">Percent</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Algeria" title="Islam in Algeria">Islam</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:green; width:97.9%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">97.9%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Unaffiliated</td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:gray; width:1.8%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.8%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Algeria" title="Christianity in Algeria">Christianity</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:blue; width:0.2%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.2%</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Algeria" title="History of the Jews in Algeria">Judaism</a></td> 
           <td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;">
            <div style="background:black; width:0.1%; overflow: hidden;">
              
            </div></td> 
           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">0.1%</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is the predominant religion in Algeria, with its adherents, mostly Sunnis, accounting for 99% of the population according to a 2012 CIA World Factbook estimate,<sup id="cite_ref-AlgeriaFactbook_95-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AlgeriaFactbook-95">[94]</a></sup> and 97.9% according to Pew Research in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-pew_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pew-151">[150]</a></sup> There are about 150,000 <a href="/wiki/Ibadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibadi">Ibadis</a> in the M'zab Valley in the region of <a href="/wiki/Ghardaia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghardaia">Ghardaia</a>. Estimates of the <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Algeria" title="Christianity in Algeria">Christian population</a> range from 60,000<sup id="cite_ref-Pew_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pew-152">[151]</a></sup> to 200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-153">[152]</a></sup> Algerian citizens who are Christians predominantly belong to <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> groups, which have seen increased pressure from the government in recent years including many forced closures.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-auto_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-153">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Algeria has given the <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> world a number of prominent thinkers, including <a href="/wiki/Emir_Abdelkader" title="Emir Abdelkader">Emir Abdelkader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdelhamid_Ben_Badis" title="Abdelhamid Ben Badis">Abdelhamid Ben Badis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mouloud_Kacem_Na%C3%AEt_Belkacem" title="Mouloud Kacem Naît Belkacem">Mouloud Kacem Naît Belkacem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malek_Bennabi" title="Malek Bennabi">Malek Bennabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Arkoun" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohamed Arkoun">Mohamed Arkoun</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Algeria" title="Health in Algeria">Health in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2002, Algeria had inadequate numbers of physicians (1.13 per 1,000 people), nurses (2.23 per 1,000 people), and dentists (0.31 per 1,000 people). Access to "improved water sources" was limited to 92% of the population in urban areas and 80% of the population in the rural areas. Some 99% of Algerians living in urban areas, but only 82% of those living in rural areas, had access to "improved sanitation". According to the World Bank, Algeria is making progress toward its goal of "reducing by half the number of people without sustainable access to improved drinking water and basic sanitation by 2015". Given Algeria's young population, policy favors preventive health care and clinics over hospitals. In keeping with this policy, the government maintains an immunization program. However, poor sanitation and unclean water still cause <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hepatitis" title="Hepatitis">hepatitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Typhoid_fever" title="Typhoid fever">typhoid fever</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dysentery" title="Dysentery">dysentery</a>. The poor generally receive health care free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Health records have been maintained in Algeria since 1882 and began adding Muslims living in the south to their vital record database in 1905 during French rule.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Algeria" title="Education in Algeria">Education in Algeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Algeria" title="List of universities in Algeria">List of universities in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg/220px-Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg/330px-Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg/440px-Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3780" data-file-height="2598"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Des_%C3%A9levesen_Alg%C3%A9rie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Algerian school children
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since the 1970s, in a centralised system that was designed to significantly reduce the rate of illiteracy, the Algerian government introduced a decree by which school attendance became compulsory for all children aged between 6 and 15 years who have the ability to track their learning through the 20 facilities built since independence, now the literacy rate is around 78.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-illit_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illit-157">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png/220px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png/330px-UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png 2x" data-file-width="397" data-file-height="314"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UIS_Literacy_Rate_Algeria_population_plus15_1980_2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/UNESCO_Institute_for_Statistics" title="UNESCO Institute for Statistics">UIS</a> literacy rate Algeria population plus 15 1985–2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1972, Arabic is used as the language of instruction during the first nine years of schooling. From the third year, French is taught and it is also the language of instruction for science classes. The students can also learn English, Italian, Spanish and German. In 2008, new programs at the elementary appeared, therefore the compulsory schooling does not start at the age of six anymore, but at the age of five.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> Apart from the 122 private schools, the Universities of the State are free of charge. After nine years of primary school, students can go to the high school or to an educational institution. The school offers two programs: general or technical. At the end of the third year of secondary school, students pass the exam of the baccalaureate, which allows once it is successful to pursue graduate studies in universities and institutes.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Education is officially compulsory for children between the ages of six and 15. In 2008, the illiteracy rate for people over 10 was 22.3%, 15.6% for men and 29.0% for women. The province with the lowest rate of illiteracy was <a href="/wiki/Algiers_Province" title="Algiers Province">Algiers Province</a> at 11.6%, while the province with the highest rate was <a href="/wiki/Djelfa_Province" title="Djelfa Province">Djelfa Province</a> at 35.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-illit_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illit-157">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Algeria has 26 universities and 67 institutions of higher education, which must accommodate a million Algerians and 80,000 foreign students in 2008. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Algiers" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Algiers">University of Algiers</a>, founded in 1879, is the oldest, it offers education in various disciplines (law, medicine, science and letters). 25 of these universities and almost all of the institutions of higher education were founded after the independence of the country. </p>
      <p>Even if some of them offer instruction in <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> like areas of law and the economy, most of the other sectors as science and medicine continue to be provided in French and English. Among the most important universities, there are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sciences_and_Technology_Houari_Boumediene" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Sciences and Technology Houari Boumediene">University of Sciences and Technology Houari Boumediene</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Mentouri" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Mentouri">University of Mentouri</a> Constantine, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oran" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Oran">University of Oran</a> Es-Senia. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Abou_Bekr_Belka%C3%AFd" title="University of Abou Bekr Belkaïd">University of Abou Bekr Belkaïd</a> in Tlemcen and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Batna" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Batna">University of Batna</a> Hadj Lakhdar occupy the 26th and 45th row in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities">Cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Algeria" title="List of cities in Algeria">List of cities in Algeria</a>
      </div>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Algeria" title="Culture of Algeria">Culture of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bensari2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bensari2.jpg/220px-Bensari2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bensari2.jpg/330px-Bensari2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Bensari2.jpg/440px-Bensari2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1724" data-file-height="1189"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bensari2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Algerian musicians in <a href="/wiki/Tlemcen" title="Tlemcen">Tlemcen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Algeria" title="Ottoman Algeria">Ottoman Algeria</a>. Painting by <a href="/wiki/Bachir_Yell%C3%A8s" title="Bachir Yellès">Bachir Yellès</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Modern Algerian literature, split between <a href="/wiki/Classical_Arabic" title="Classical Arabic">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Tamazight</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="French Language">French</a>, has been strongly influenced by the country's recent history. <a href="/wiki/List_of_Algerian_writers" title="List of Algerian writers">Famous novelists</a> of the 20th century include <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Dib" title="Mohammed Dib">Mohammed Dib</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus">Albert Camus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kateb_Yacine" title="Kateb Yacine">Kateb Yacine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ahlam_Mosteghanemi" title="Ahlam Mosteghanemi">Ahlam Mosteghanemi</a> while <a href="/wiki/Assia_Djebar" title="Assia Djebar">Assia Djebar</a> is widely translated. Among the important novelists of the 1980s were <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Mimouni" title="Rachid Mimouni">Rachid Mimouni</a>, later vice-president of <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tahar_Djaout" title="Tahar Djaout">Tahar Djaout</a>, murdered by an <a href="/wiki/Islamist" class="mw-redirect" title="Islamist">Islamist</a> group in 1993 for his secularist views.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malek_Bennabi" title="Malek Bennabi">Malek Bennabi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Frantz_Fanon" title="Frantz Fanon">Frantz Fanon</a> are noted for their thoughts on <a href="/wiki/Decolonization" title="Decolonization">decolonization</a>; <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Tagaste" class="mw-redirect" title="Tagaste">Tagaste</a> (modern-day <a href="/wiki/Souk_Ahras" title="Souk Ahras">Souk Ahras</a>); and <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun" title="Ibn Khaldun">Ibn Khaldun</a>, though born in <a href="/wiki/Tunis" title="Tunis">Tunis</a>, wrote the <a href="/wiki/Muqaddima" class="mw-redirect" title="Muqaddima">Muqaddima</a> while staying in Algeria. The works of the <a href="/wiki/Senussi" class="mw-redirect" title="Senussi">Sanusi</a> family in pre-colonial times, and of <a href="/wiki/Emir_Abdelkader" title="Emir Abdelkader">Emir Abdelkader</a> and Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Abdelhamid_Ben_Badis" title="Abdelhamid Ben Badis">Ben Badis</a> in colonial times, are widely noted. The Latin author <a href="/wiki/Apuleius" title="Apuleius">Apuleius</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Madaurus" class="mw-redirect" title="Madaurus">Madaurus</a> (Mdaourouch), in what later became Algeria. </p>
      <p>Contemporary <a href="/wiki/Algerian_cinema" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian cinema">Algerian cinema</a> is various in terms of genre, exploring a wider range of themes and issues. There has been a transition from cinema which focused on the war of independence to films more concerned with the everyday lives of Algerians.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Algeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Algeria">Media of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:163px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Portrait-racim.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3a/Portrait-racim.jpg" decoding="async" width="161" height="231" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="161" data-file-height="231"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Portrait-racim.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mohammed Racim was a painter and founder of the Algerian school of miniature painting
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Algerian painters, like <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mohamed_Racim" class="extiw" title="fr:Mohamed Racim">Mohamed Racim</a> or Baya, attempted to revive the prestigious Algerian past prior to French colonization, at the same time that they have contributed to the preservation of the authentic values of Algeria. In this line, <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Temam" title="Mohamed Temam">Mohamed Temam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdelkhader_Houamel" title="Abdelkhader Houamel">Abdelkhader Houamel</a> have also returned through this art, scenes from the history of the country, the habits and customs of the past and the country life. Other new artistic currents including the one of <a href="/wiki/M%27hamed_Issiakhem" title="M'hamed Issiakhem">M'hamed Issiakhem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Khadda" title="Mohammed Khadda">Mohammed Khadda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bachir_Yelles" class="mw-redirect" title="Bachir Yelles">Bachir Yelles</a>, appeared on the scene of Algerian painting, abandoning figurative classical painting to find new pictorial ways, in order to adapt Algerian paintings to the new realities of the country through its struggle and its aspirations. <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Khadda" title="Mohammed Khadda">Mohammed Khadda</a><sup id="cite_ref-art_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art-164">[163]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/M%27hamed_Issiakhem" title="M'hamed Issiakhem">M'hamed Issiakhem</a> have been notable in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-art_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art-164">[163]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Algerian_literature" title="Algerian literature">Algerian literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Algerian_writers" title="List of Algerian writers">List of Algerian writers</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG/220px-Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="258" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG/330px-Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG/440px-Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1688" data-file-height="1981"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ahlem_Mosteghanemi_at_Beirut_Book_Fair_2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Ahlam_Mosteghanemi" title="Ahlam Mosteghanemi">Ahlam Mosteghanemi</a>, the most widely read woman writer in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The historic roots of Algerian literature go back to the <a href="/wiki/Numidia" title="Numidia">Numidian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa_(Roman_province)" title="Africa (Roman province)">Roman African</a> era, when <a href="/wiki/Apuleius" title="Apuleius">Apuleius</a> wrote <i><a href="/wiki/The_Golden_Ass" title="The Golden Ass">The Golden Ass</a></i>, the only Latin novel to survive in its entirety. This period had also known <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonius_Marcellus" title="Nonius Marcellus">Nonius Marcellus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martianus_Capella" title="Martianus Capella">Martianus Capella</a>, among many others. The Middle Ages have known many Arabic writers who revolutionized the Arab world literature, with authors like <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_al-Buni" title="Ahmad al-Buni">Ahmad al-Buni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Manzur" title="Ibn Manzur">Ibn Manzur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ibn_Khaldoun" class="mw-redirect" title="Ibn Khaldoun">Ibn Khaldoun</a>, who wrote the <a href="/wiki/Muqaddimah" title="Muqaddimah">Muqaddimah</a> while staying in Algeria, and many others. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus">Albert Camus</a> was an Algerian-born French Pied-Noir author. In 1957 he was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Prize in literature">Nobel Prize in literature</a>. </p> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:248px;max-width:248px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:122px;max-width:122px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus,_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27,_published_in_1825_(C19).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg/120px-Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="155" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg/180px-Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg/240px-Lucius_Apuleius_Platonicus%2C_from_%27Crabbes_Historical_Dictionary%27%2C_published_in_1825_%28C19%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="558" data-file-height="719"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Apuleius" title="Apuleius">Apuleius</a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:122px;max-width:122px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg/120px-Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg" decoding="async" width="120" height="148" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg/180px-Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg/240px-Kateb_Yacine_Nedjma_authograph.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1627" data-file-height="2008"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Kateb_Yacine" title="Kateb Yacine">Kateb Yacine</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Today Algeria contains, in its literary landscape, big names having not only marked the Algerian literature, but also the universal literary heritage in Arabic and French. </p>
      <p>As a first step, Algerian literature was marked by works whose main concern was the assertion of the Algerian national entity, there is the publication of novels as the <i>Algerian trilogy</i> of <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Dib" title="Mohammed Dib">Mohammed Dib</a>, or even <i>Nedjma</i> of <a href="/wiki/Kateb_Yacine" title="Kateb Yacine">Kateb Yacine</a> novel which is often regarded as a monumental and major work. Other known writers will contribute to the emergence of Algerian literature whom include <a href="/wiki/Mouloud_Feraoun" title="Mouloud Feraoun">Mouloud Feraoun</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malek_Bennabi" title="Malek Bennabi">Malek Bennabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malek_Haddad" title="Malek Haddad">Malek Haddad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moufdi_Zakaria" title="Moufdi Zakaria">Moufdi Zakaria</a>, Abdelhamid Ben Badis, Mohamed Laïd Al-Khalifa, <a href="/wiki/Mouloud_Mammeri" title="Mouloud Mammeri">Mouloud Mammeri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frantz_Fanon" title="Frantz Fanon">Frantz Fanon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Assia_Djebar" title="Assia Djebar">Assia Djebar</a>. </p>
      <p>In the aftermath of the independence, several new authors emerged on the Algerian literary scene, they will attempt through their works to expose a number of social problems, among them there are <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Boudjedra" title="Rachid Boudjedra">Rachid Boudjedra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Mimouni" title="Rachid Mimouni">Rachid Mimouni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leila_Sebbar" class="mw-redirect" title="Leila Sebbar">Leila Sebbar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahar_Djaout" title="Tahar Djaout">Tahar Djaout</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tahir_Wattar" class="mw-redirect" title="Tahir Wattar">Tahir Wattar</a>. </p>
      <p>Currently, a part of Algerian writers tends to be defined in a literature of shocking expression, due to the terrorism that occurred during the 1990s, the other party is defined in a different style of literature who staged an individualistic conception of the human adventure. Among the most noted recent works, there is the writer, <i>the swallows of Kabul</i> and <i>the attack</i> of <a href="/wiki/Yasmina_Khadra" title="Yasmina Khadra">Yasmina Khadra</a>, <i>the oath of barbarians</i> of <a href="/wiki/Boualem_Sansal" title="Boualem Sansal">Boualem Sansal</a>, <i>memory of the flesh</i> of <a href="/wiki/Ahlam_Mosteghanemi" title="Ahlam Mosteghanemi">Ahlam Mosteghanemi</a> and the last novel by Assia Djebar <i>nowhere in my father's House</i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Algeria" title="Music of Algeria">Music of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Anka.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Anka.jpg/170px-Anka.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Anka.jpg/255px-Anka.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Anka.jpg/340px-Anka.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1326" data-file-height="1729"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Anka.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/El_Hadj_M%27Hamed_El_Anka" title="El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka">El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Chaabi_(Algeria)" title="Chaabi (Algeria)">Chaâbi music</a> is a typically Algerian musical genre characterized by specific rhythms and of Qacidate (popular poems) in Arabic dialect. The undisputed master of this music is <a href="/wiki/El_Hadj_M%27Hamed_El_Anka" title="El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka">El Hadj M'Hamed El Anka</a>. The Constantinois <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_classical_music" title="Andalusian classical music">Malouf</a> style is saved by musician from whom <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Tahar_Fergani" title="Mohamed Tahar Fergani">Mohamed Tahar Fergani</a> is a performer. </p>
      <p>Folk music styles include <a href="/wiki/Bedouin_music" title="Bedouin music">Bedouin music</a>, characterized by the poetic songs based on long kacida (poems); Kabyle music, based on a rich repertoire that is poetry and old tales passed through generations; Shawiya music, a folklore from diverse areas of the <a href="/wiki/Aur%C3%A8s_Mountains" title="Aurès Mountains">Aurès Mountains</a>. Rahaba music style is unique to the Aures. <a href="/wiki/Souad_Massi" title="Souad Massi">Souad Massi</a> is a rising Algerian folk singer. Other Algerian singers of the diaspora include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Manel_Filali&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Manel Filali (page does not exist)">Manel Filali</a> in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kenza_Farah" title="Kenza Farah">Kenza Farah</a> in France. Tergui music is sung in <a href="/wiki/Tuareg_languages" title="Tuareg languages">Tuareg languages</a> generally, <a href="/wiki/Tinariwen" title="Tinariwen">Tinariwen</a> had a worldwide success. Finally, the staïfi music is born in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9tif" title="Sétif">Sétif</a> and remains a unique style of its kind. </p>
      <p>Modern music is available in several facets, <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%AF" title="Raï">Raï</a> music is a style typical of western Algeria. <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">Rap</a>, a relatively recent style in Algeria, is experiencing significant growth. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Algeria" title="Cinema of Algeria">Cinema of Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:La_battaglia_di_Algeri_screen.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/La_battaglia_di_Algeri_screen.png/280px-La_battaglia_di_Algeri_screen.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/La_battaglia_di_Algeri_screen.png/420px-La_battaglia_di_Algeri_screen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ef/La_battaglia_di_Algeri_screen.png 2x" data-file-width="498" data-file-height="254"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:La_battaglia_di_Algeri_screen.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Italian-Algerian film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Battle_of_Algiers" title="The Battle of Algiers">The Battle of Algiers</a></i> (1966) won the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Lion" title="Golden Lion">Golden Lion</a> at the <a href="/wiki/27th_Venice_International_Film_Festival" title="27th Venice International Film Festival">27th Venice International Film Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Algerian state's interest in film-industry activities can be seen in the annual budget of DZD 200 million (EUR 1.3 million) allocated to production, specific measures and an ambitious programme plan implemented by the Ministry of Culture in order to promote national production, renovate the cinema stock and remedy the weak links in distribution and exploitation. </p>
      <p>The financial support provided by the state, through the Fund for the Development of the Arts, Techniques and the Film Industry (FDATIC) and the Algerian Agency for Cultural Influence (AARC), plays a key role in the promotion of national production. Between 2007 and 2013, FDATIC subsidised 98 films (feature films, documentaries and short films). In mid-2013, AARC had already supported a total of 78 films, including 42 feature films, 6 short films and 30 documentaries. </p>
      <p>According to the European Audiovisual Observatory's LUMIERE database, 41 Algerian films were distributed in Europe between 1996 and 2013; 21 films in this repertoire were Algerian-French co-productions. <a href="/wiki/Days_of_Glory_(2006_film)" title="Days of Glory (2006 film)"><i>Days of Glory</i> (2006)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Outside_the_Law_(2010_film)" title="Outside the Law (2010 film)"><i>Outside the Law</i> (2010)</a> recorded the highest number of admissions in the European Union, 3,172,612 and 474,722, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Algeria won the <a href="/wiki/Palme_d%27Or" title="Palme d'Or">Palme d'Or</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/Chronicle_of_the_Years_of_Fire" title="Chronicle of the Years of Fire">Chronicle of the Years of Fire</a></i> (1975), two Oscars for <a href="/wiki/Z_(1969_film)" title="Z (1969 film)"><i>Z</i> (1969)</a>, and other awards for the Italian-Algerian movie <i><a href="/wiki/The_Battle_of_Algiers" title="The Battle of Algiers">The Battle of Algiers</a></i>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Algerian_cuisine" title="Algerian cuisine">Algerian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg/220px-Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg/330px-Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg/440px-Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1678"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bulgur_wheat_salad.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Bulgur" title="Bulgur">Bulgur</a>-based salad
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Algerian cuisine is rich and diverse. The country was considered as the "granary of Rome". It offers a component of dishes and varied dishes, depending on the region and according to the seasons. The cuisine uses cereals as the main products, since they are always produced with abundance in the country. There is not a dish where cereals are not present. </p>
      <p>Algerian cuisine varies from one region to another, according to seasonal vegetables. It can be prepared using meat, fish and vegetables. Among the dishes known, <a href="/wiki/Couscous" title="Couscous">couscous</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-WDL_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-168">[167]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chorba" title="Chorba">chorba</a>, rechta, chakhchoukha, berkoukes, <a href="/wiki/Shakshouka" title="Shakshouka">shakshouka</a>, mthewem, chtitha, mderbel, dolma, brik or bourek, garantita, lham'hlou, etc. <a href="/wiki/Merguez" title="Merguez">Merguez</a> sausage is widely used in Algeria, but it differs, depending on the region and on the added spices. </p>
      <p>Cakes are marketed and can be found in cities either in Algeria, in Europe or North America. However, traditional cakes are also made at home, following the habits and customs of each family. Among these cakes, there are Tamina, Baklawa, Chrik, Garn logzelles, Griouech, Kalb el-louz, Makroud, Mbardja, Mchewek, Samsa, Tcharak, Baghrir, Khfaf, Zlabia, Aarayech, Ghroubiya and Mghergchette. Algerian pastry also contains Tunisian or French cakes. Marketed and home-made bread products include varieties such as Kessra or Khmira or Harchaya, chopsticks and so-called washers Khoubz dar or Matloue. Other traditional meals sold often as street food include mhadjeb or mahjouba, karantika, doubara, chakhchoukha, hassouna, and t'chicha. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Algeria" title="Sport in Algeria">Sport in Algeria</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Various games have existed in Algeria since antiquity. In the <a href="/wiki/Aur%C3%A8s_Mountains" title="Aurès Mountains">Aures</a>, people played several games such as El Kherba or El khergueba (<a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a> variant). Playing cards, <a href="/wiki/Checkers" class="mw-redirect" title="Checkers">checkers</a> and chess games are part of Algerian culture. Racing (<a href="/wiki/Fantasia_(culture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fantasia (culture)">fantasia</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Rifle_shooting" class="mw-redirect" title="Rifle shooting">rifle shooting</a> are part of cultural recreation of the Algerians.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first Algerian and African gold medalist is <a href="/wiki/Boughera_El_Ouafi" title="Boughera El Ouafi">Boughera El Ouafi</a> in <a href="/wiki/1928_Summer_Olympics" title="1928 Summer Olympics">1928 Olympics of Amsterdam</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Marathon" title="Marathon">Marathon</a>. The second Algerian Medalist was <a href="/wiki/Alain_Mimoun" title="Alain Mimoun">Alain Mimoun</a> in <a href="/wiki/1956_Summer_Olympics" title="1956 Summer Olympics">1956 Summer Olympics</a> in Melbourne. Several men and women were champions in athletics in the 1990s including <a href="/wiki/Noureddine_Morceli" title="Noureddine Morceli">Noureddine Morceli</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hassiba_Boulmerka" title="Hassiba Boulmerka">Hassiba Boulmerka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nouria_M%C3%A9rah-Benida" title="Nouria Mérah-Benida">Nouria Merah-Benida</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taoufik_Makhloufi" title="Taoufik Makhloufi">Taoufik Makhloufi</a>, all specialized in <a href="/wiki/Middle-distance_running" title="Middle-distance running">middle-distance running</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Football_in_Algeria" title="Football in Algeria">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Algeria. Several names are engraved in the history of the sport, including <a href="/wiki/Lakhdar_Belloumi" title="Lakhdar Belloumi">Lakhdar Belloumi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachid_Mekhloufi" title="Rachid Mekhloufi">Rachid Mekhloufi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hac%C3%A8ne_Lalmas" title="Hacène Lalmas">Hassen Lalmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rabah_Madjer" title="Rabah Madjer">Rabah Madjer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salah_Assad" title="Salah Assad">Salah Assad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Djamel_Zidane" title="Djamel Zidane">Djamel Zidane</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Algeria_national_football_team" title="Algeria national football team">Algeria national football team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 FIFA World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 FIFA World Cup</a>, <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a> and <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2014 FIFA World Cup">2014 FIFA World Cup</a>. In addition, several football clubs have won continental and international trophies as the club <a href="/wiki/ES_S%C3%A9tif" title="ES Sétif">ES Sétif</a> or <a href="/wiki/JS_Kabylia" class="mw-redirect" title="JS Kabylia">JS Kabylia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Football_Federation" title="Algerian Football Federation">Algerian Football Federation</a> is an association of Algeria football clubs organizing national competitions and international matches of the selection of Algeria national football team.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Algeria&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <i><a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a></i> states that about 15% of Algerians, a minority, identify as Berber even though many Algerians have Berber origins. The Factbook explains that of the approximately 15% who identify as Berber, most live in the <a href="/wiki/Kabylia" title="Kabylia">Kabylia</a> region, more closely identify with Berber heritage instead of Arab heritage, and are Muslim.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
